O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, most noble sons, I have completed this book which is the back of the science of medicine, filling it up together with its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is guarded in our region and is restricted from all things, it has perished the science and been lost, and there remains nothing but the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and the minds are closed and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I can revive it together with the order of this treatment according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of cauterizing irons and other tools of the work with the assistance of declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is appropriate for someone who undertakes this to study the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations of all, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and sinews and the number of veins, and the flow and movements of blood and its rest, and the source of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because Hippocrates says that with the left hand it is not very good, and with the right hand it is little; and equally in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that those who are not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, if they attempt to perform it, may make mistakes and harm people; thus I have often seen many of these who interfere with this science and abandon their own.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish woman who lanced an abscess of the neck or breast of a woman, and lanced the arteries of the neck; because so much blood issued out that the woman died between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And another case treated a man of age, and the arrow was large; it carried away with it a piece of the intestine, and died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat it, and saw the position of the wound and the size of the arrow, and if they cut it, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case where the Duke of our land took care of himself who had broken his leg, and with the breaker he got a wound; and the nurse in ignorance kept the fracture above the wound with splints for a long time, and did not let any salve on the wound, and so it ended; and he commanded that it not be moved; and so it remained until the leg was completely infected and the foot and came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and he urged me to come to dislocate his leg; and when I heard it dislocated, it was in the countryside and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the ways of the corruption were already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not stop spreading throughout the limb until the limb was entirely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another way that would burst the abscess and become infected, and then inflame due to the evil of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a pus, when it is free from melancholic humor, does not need much if only touched with iron if it is not in the joint where one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you should know that work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is, where he has danger in many positions; and I will show in each part of this book where he has fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For why it is important that you guard yourself, so that the wicked may not speak evil of you if you take up your weapons in battle, and undertake your maladies firmly and steadfastly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to safety and are healed; and leave behind the contagious diseases of great sickness; and remove your weapons from what makes you doubtful, and be such that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen advises in some of his warnings: 'Do not take on the care of seriously ill patients unless you are called a wise man.'
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatment according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, and the chapters are ordered from the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and about the materials of cauteries, and about everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and incising, and about wounds, and about the extraction of arrows, and about similar things; and the chapters are ordered and about the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered from the highest to the lowest, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we remember the work, it is necessary that I mention the quality of the help and harm of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest and most subtle science and secret knowledge; and because of this, many wise people spoke about it and agreed on it; and I do not speak much about it, because I make it long.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally in all conditions where there is matter, whether the condition is hot with matter or dry without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry weather, they all agreed that the fire cauterization was great help; and the others said the opposite: that the fire cauterization was only helpful for diseases coming from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured by heat or dryness; and those who said the opposite claimed that cauterization was great help for hot and dry diseases that come from people.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and its moisture to the hot fire, you cool the body.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any way, no one should interfere except those who have experienced it, and who know the chapter on cauteries from long use, and the diversity of men's constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the remedies and the space of time; for other constitutions we do not fear, specifically in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the patients gathered and agreed to the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my sons, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater benefit than cauterization with hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	The flesh is simple, and only comes to the member that is cooked, and does not harm other members unless it has a name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fiery medicines come from one member to another by moving away, and bring diseases of the body to the affected member; and perhaps the evil flesh for its high cost and the goodness of its substance does not cause harm, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this by experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it has been above the truth of things; and because I do not like to speak at length, for I only want to give you the secret which is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, how it destroys diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they should be done in what manner the cautery is to be made, and ask when seeking.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cautery is beneficial in all times, because the harmful things that come from it are removed by the help of the cautery; and indeed, if the cautery is for necessary pain, not only for short-term but also for long-term, which cannot wait until the greatest harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think, my son, like the foolish people; for the disease that is healed by cautery has no return; and they say it thus, but it is not so because cautery is only medicine that moves the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and is as good a medicine for its quick effect, and for the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And another thing is that the disease comes not always according to the condition of the humor and the body of the disease and its power; and it is assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of meats and similar things, if not cauteries are administered in him where he has little superfluity and moisture, as cauteries of dense for the pain, and similar things, and the pain does not return much; but it is little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and it is seen; but they do not believe that cauteries work after medicine, but their intentions are false, and it is cauteries the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth it.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is important to understand that cauterization is a part of medicine, not merely according to the intentions of those who are misguided.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that a cauterizing instrument of gold is more effective than iron, and they only said this because of the quality of gold and the high value of its substance; and they said that the effects of cautery do not cause harm, but I have found that this is not true, as I have experienced it, and it can be seen in some people; and a cauterizing instrument of gold is more effective than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And in any case, when you heat the gold instrument, you should not be concerned about its color changing due to the heat, and it has been previously cooled; and if it is heated too much, they put it into the fire; and thus it has enough protection.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use the fire cautery that we have already prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you would order this chapter on the shoulders first, for it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The oil cauterizer
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterizer is used for moisture and cold on the head, and it is done for two reasons: due to a disease called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the shoulder to the ears, and for multiple symptoms and tooth pain, and throat pain, and for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, and apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the hairs should be removed by medicinal solution, changing the skin III or IV times, according to the virtues and age and custom of the hair, so that it can bear it; and then repeat the head of the hair.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then let him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on top of the palm; after that, put the root of your thumb over the root of his nail between his two eyes; and where your fingers come together, if it bleeds from the center, then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the bone in its socket with ink, and gently pull and stretch your hand little by little; then slowly release your hand, and reward the bone if you see the bone is small; and if you do not see it, then start the cauterization again until you see the bone as I have told you; after take a little rope, and put in warm and soft cotton inside, and place on the bone, and let it stay for three days; after put on a moist cloth in butter; and leave it until the burn is healed; afterwards treat the wound called «tetrafarmaçon» until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old ones said, that the longer one stays with the wound open, the more it purges; and for this reason it helps to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one should cauterize the wound so much that a part of the bone is burned, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it is healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the others said that one should cauterize the wound less strongly above, and put in as much as one removes from the bone as wide as the vermilion that women put in their hair to make the humors come out easily; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards it should be healed and sealed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be entirely good in all cases, except for those who have a fear of pain; and I think that I should leave it; because the affected parts are weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and even when the affected part is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is safer and milder for me, and from this use I operate in such cases.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the main
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in all cases the main pain comes with chronic pain that lasts a long time, one should use the affected parts and pills called "cochie", and purging of head and eyes and plasters; and if one does the cauterization that we have already mentioned, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care not to burn the patient with this cautery, as it is of a very hot nature, and not too quickly; therefore, apply it in a controlled manner as we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After applying the cautery to each of the horns of the head up to the bone, as we have mentioned before, and applying the cauterizing iron called "vassals"; and place the vacuum in the parts where you apply the suction; raise your hand so that you do not touch the bone: the pain from this cautery is much greater than from others, and I will speak about it later; and it is necessary that the cauterizing of the horns be more subtle than the one used to cauterize the middle of the head, and its form is:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cauterization
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When a sudden pain comes to a part of the head, and the disease spreads to the eye, and the patient is purged by changing medicines, and the other treatments that I have mentioned in the division of diseases do not help: then you must cauterize it in two ways, namely with medicine or fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with medicine is done by holding a hot iron and scraping off the skin and then applying it to the eye for a short time, and then making the temple in such a way that you can replace the iron outside the skin; and when it is replaced, hold it tightly and steadily for twelve hours; then remove it and treat it with a cotton swab soaked in honey for two or three days; then apply a poultice of bread soaked in warm water.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment as long as they are healthy; and if you see that it is of some medicinal substances that I have written or prescribe to treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cauterization is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cauterization with this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the form of a cloth or it has a small hook, and in the middle a small appearance; and place it on the painful part, and hold your hand and turn the iron slightly, until half of the hot substance is gone; and release your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is before, and let out abundant blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton on a sling around the limb for three days; then place moistened cotton on the wound, and cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this wound with the cauterizing iron called "cultellare", apply it at the point, and be careful not to cover the artery in this wound which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the wound
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat the wound as we have mentioned in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauterizing iron before mentioned does not cause much pain or heat, then it is necessary to extinguish the cauterizing iron called "cultellare" until it is white; and also place a line of half an inch of cloth on the limb, and take your hand once, and be careful not to cover the artery and that no blood comes out to the bone; and be careful of the mandible that does not move when turned, and the nerves have only sight of the moved and that spasm does not cause pain, and be careful of the bleeding of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting it causes great fear and immediately to that which is not known, and which is not studied and experienced; and leave the work in this way; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding of blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If you see that this fire cauterization does not suffice for the disease, and the patient is in pain, cauterize it with the head of the chief as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said or from the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cauterization that has two knives; and this fire cauterization is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from cold, and medicines have been applied and other treatments as we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then warm this cauterization called "poins", of which is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pricking all around the ear, where the pain is located on both sides, and moving away a little from the root of the ear until you have signed the earlobe; then apply X poins around each ear; after that, cure the earlobes as long as they are healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that should be cured by cauterization is only those that move from the mouth, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not apply cauterization to similar things that come from choking and spitting out blood.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you encounter this appearance of torture that prevents the flow of water from the ear and the mouth, and it does not improve, then it is necessary to cauterize the pain with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, and the other a little further from the temple, and the third in the corner of the mouth; and place the cautery in the part that opens healthily, and make the cauterization above a little behind the ear, and another in the temple as far as a pinch; and leave the cautery so high that half of the face is burned; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it resembles the cauterizing tool that we have placed before, but it is a bit more subtle and it requires that the knife be a bit larger; after healing the wound as I have mentioned earlier, as long as they are healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is an old condition and you treat it as we have mentioned earlier, and it does not improve, and the pain does not have fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two corners of the head, and one on the forehead, and one on the back of the mouth of the stomach; and treat them as we have mentioned earlier.
de litargie	For laziness, do not delay in applying
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large and modified brains; then, after removing the entire head, place the mustard plaster on the occipital region, as written or described in the treatment of plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: if you do so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is thus healthy, it is good; but if not, make three cauterizations on the head by descending towards the neck, and leave a space of one inch between each cauterization; and the cure is as with the others, and if you have seen that they are suffering, make one cauterization in the middle; and if the matter is, two more above the two horns, and the cure until it is healthy; and let the cauterizations be called "olivare" as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to clean the head of years and mucus that we have previously mentioned; after that, heat the head of the pain, then cauterize it and each horn, and behind and three times above the spine of the neck; and if you have more trouble, and the body is wet and the pains are suffering, and the disease is outside, if you do four cauterizations above the spine of the back; and let it be so long as the most helpful is arrived, and release your hand; after the cure until it is healed, and let the cauterizations that are called "olivare" that we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should not use cauterization except for those who are fleamatic, and it is first necessary to modify the brain of years and other treatments that we have said in the division when the injuries are great and suffer from painful medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot suffer, make them gargle and chew often with good meats; after that, let the head rest in the middle, and then apply cauterization as we have said before, and cauterize on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the injuries are far and painful, apply cauterization as I have said to those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterization be olive oil according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the pain is severe, then apply the delicate cauterization as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy, there are excessive or corrupted moisture and large fluids, then use the cauterizing tool as we have mentioned for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy, the excessive or corrupted moisture is declining towards melancholy, and the wound is moist with the bad humor, then give it something to drink that cleanses the brain, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After removing the head of the wound; after making a good tortoise shell-shaped bandage, as a circle, and putting it on the head; and the pain decreases, and it is well held from all parts; present the liniment, and it should be mixed with old beeswax; and heat it gently over fire, so that the patient can bear it; then remove the circle from inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the wound every week once with good management until it is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	When you see the fire cautery being performed by making many pricks with the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the brain, and then places cotton soaked in butter and chicken grease on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the pain of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When pain comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient a bad thing mundifying the head, and keep it from all moisture, and make it sweat or bathe it many times with fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Then command the patient to turn his head, and perform the cauterization on the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples simultaneously, or if one descends from the pain is in one; and cover all the cautery with all the veins and arteries that are outside the skull, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and keep from the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with a sponge.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of veins and in the incision, how to perform it; and never cauterize or heat anything outside the two lower bones.
dou cors des larmes	The path of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are above the veins, or behind the arteries that are in the appearance of the main one; and it is seen that it is superfluous cold phlegm, then apply the cautery that I have mentioned at the beginning of this chapter: I cauterize the forehead, and II cauterize above the two temples, and II cauterize outside the two lower bones; and if there is more, then cauterize wisely above the sore with every small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you apply the medicine as we have mentioned in the previous section, and it does not work, then drink three doses of bad-tasting herbs; afterwards, the patient should be bled, and then cauterize or cauterize with a heated iron; and apply two cautery burns called «clavilis» above the two sores, a little outside the cheeks; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called «clavilis»:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterizing of this cauterization, which is called "olive,
de coi ci est li forme:	is formed thus:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you have made two cauterizations on the two sorbips as long as they are; and do not leave the hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hairs that do not touch the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	It never happens that the hairs of the oil are converted to parchment, and they touch the oil, and then one makes two cauterizations according to two ways: that is to say, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

After cauterizing the figure that you have marked a little and not too many times, where the curse is located; and the signs of health of the work are that you see the paper retreating, and the hairs raised to the point of the oil; then light your hand, and let it be so for three hours, then put moistened cotton on the burn until the blister is opened; after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come back, and the paper is softened, then restart the cauterization on the same leg, as you did first; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural level, and is even, and do not prick at the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fire cautery is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then take a piece of parchment in the shape of a mint leaf; then take French soap and live copper, one of each, and grind them together well; and apply it strongly, so that it does not cool, then spread it on the form you have made like the mint leaf, and put it on the paper of the eyes; and if the patient's disease is only in one eye, then open the other, and do the same; and put some cotton moistened with oil behind the ear; and the one who has the disease should be in a healthy state and show the medicine above, and press the poultice every time the patient feels the medicine biting, for it feels biting like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take the medicine at your own discretion.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the burn is healed, lift the limb from the pain, and if you see the paper raised as it was raised by constraint of fire or incision; and if so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then continue to apply the medicine on the limb or where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes are steady; then put on a moistened cotton pad until the wound is cleaned, after which care the limb of the burn which is called «dyafenis» and others, until they are healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you have the task to stay well in your work by great care that you do not cut into the medicine with those.

Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And since the eyes of men are different in size and smallness, and according to what you are constrained; and do not reply with the right way to that one who is studied in this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistulas by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not work, then it is necessary for you to cauterize them in this way.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place his head in your safe hands; and tie the bandage on his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor does it dislodge his head; afterwards put cotton moistened with water or urine at the tip of the cauterizer: and heat the cauterizer which is near the head as if it were the form of a quill pen, similarly the one that is the cauterizer; if you see, if it is appointed from one head to the other, and if you see, if it is also like a tent; but all the same, this which is fastened is good for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it is opened and the pus is removed and dried; if it is closed, open it and remove the puss from outside; afterwards, apply the cautery hot and firmly, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the neck above the oil, so that your hand does not burn; and apply the cautery in the oil grease, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just at the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then start the cautery again and if you have the skill, and leave it for three days; afterwards, apply moist cotton in butter, and the ointment of desiccating until it is healed, and if forty days pass before it is healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is discovered; and the king according to what he would come in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a certain method of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	To the fistula, and the limb; after put in the wound a subtle powder of copper:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make of the quantity of a .З. of copper; and hold your hand firmly, and the hairs do not move, that the copper does not burn to its oil; and it is necessary to put above the oil on the hair cotton moistened with a few drops or in awe: the copper if the limb of the fistula, and the healthy by marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then you must administer purgatives to the nose, and bring the fistula back to the center of the nose as it should be in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cracked lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are cracked lips that are called "hair", and also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have mentioned in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then apply a small cauterizing needle according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the patient in those cracks until he comes just before the event; after care, the broken bone is set as soon as it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the groin
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes at the root of the groin or in the urethra, or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has rotted and fermented and aged and becomes a fistula; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, but it does not improve: therefore it is necessary that you use cauterization according to the quantity of the fistula; after plugging or puncturing the fistula, and holding your hand until the hot iron comes to the end of the limb, and behind the limb; and do so once or twice, then cure as we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to expose the limb and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines but it does not work, then place the hot iron in your healthy hand; after heating the cautery in a certain way as you would put a thorn on the tooth; and place the hot cautery deeply into the gums, holding your hand steady so that the pain feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and restart the cautery according to your will; afterwards fill the mouth with salt water, and let the person rest for an hour.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in a similar manner, the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the gum softened by being held is hardened, and the moisture corrupted is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain from the teeth comes from coldness, or there is cold or wind, and medical treatments do not work, then it is necessary to use cauterization in two ways: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter is such that you take butter from milk, and the tip in a iron or brass spoon; afterwards take cotton and wrap it over the point of a tent, and moisten it in hot butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it until it is cooled; and thus do often enough until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that moistened wool and cotton in hot butter is put on the aching tooth, and put on the heated iron until the fire comes to the movement of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery should be made of fire that is such that you hold a hot iron or brass instrument, and it should be large enough that the heat does not reach the mouth of the wound; after heating the cautery, because the shape will come out later, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, because the pain will be as great the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the wound fills its mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then remove it; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a fire cautery with the point you desire, and according to what you have available; and it is in the form of a cane:
des scrophules	of reeds
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the reeds are wet and cold, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the fire cautery with two openings for the fumes to escape from the other side; and place the cautery hot above the abscess once, or as often as it approaches the edge of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it for three days; and place soft cotton moistened in butter on top until the burn is healed; after care with ointments and tents until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the spine:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary to first empty the hairs by medicines in solution; afterwards, apply cauterization at the root of the throat, and be careful not to come too close to the throat, and do not burn too much but with a small amount.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, apply another cauterization at the joint of the neck to the top of the spine, and let the cauterizations that are called "clavicles" because of which we have the form in front; and cure the limb as we have described before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the mouth
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the disease of pormon are moisture cold, and the maladies have no fever or sweat, and is the ancient disease, then make two cauteries on the forceps in their sight; and the other cautery goes between the breasts; and let the cauteries which is called «clavile» according to the form that is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make cauteries by holding the whole cautery which is called «poins» because of the form that is above in the disease of the ears; and let the poins be just thirty, or around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment, the patient should be as follows:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cauteries are lighter, because you make three at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, shave the hairs on their back and on their side; afterwards, relieve the pain in the tender part with your right hand; and if the joint is misaligned inside, heat the cauteries that have two needles as follows:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the wound until it pierces just to the side, and bring four cauteries together with the cauterizing iron that has three needles; and for this reason, cauterization is done with the cauterizing iron that has three needles, because the shape of cauterization is these four needles; and they are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never place them above this one nerve because it has eight needles.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After place the cauterizing iron across with silk; after rest the wound, and do not move the limbs by length until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, it happens infrequently, then make the fire above the thick edge of the cauterizer, or many of the cauterizers in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and it is bound with moisture and is healed from the pain.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture come to the stomach until it reaches its normal condition, and they multiply the diarrhea in him, and are customary ways of cures and he does not improve, then it is necessary that the pain be soothed above his back, and extends his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After this, perform three cautery burns after the scoop of the least amount by the quantity of one dou, to all the cautery clavile, and two cautery burns afterwards the two ribs until the figure of the cautery is at three angles, and has equal space between them so that they are not joined together as they will go through perforation; and let the cautery be so that it does not press the two parts of the chest, and let the figure of the cautery be according to this form without jostling:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see that the cautery is burning in the stomach according to this form; and the one who has fear of this cautery, cauterizes by pinching and holding above the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you have seen of enche; then cauterize the whole cautery which is called «poins».
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the cure that we have had before, as long as they are healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes with pain from heat and moisture and great inflammation, as long as it is not removed from its natural condition by excess; and the pains are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help him much, then it is necessary that the pains be supported above his abdomen; and the sign of three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity over the liver, beyond the hypochondres, where the neck of the ox comes; and there should be space between each cauterization the thickness of a thumb; and let the cauterization be as long as the length of the body, and do not press much with your hand at all the cauterization; and let it rest only the half of the patient, and let the pains lie on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish to cauterize these cuts with a heated instrument, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and you guard that you do not burn too much of the body, for you would make it stiffer all over; and that it does not come near boiling, for the flesh is very delicate there, and the wounds to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When it has an abscess in the liver, and you see whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the mesh: if it is in the flesh, it does not hurt too much; and if it is in the mesh, it hurts greatly.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure is done, it is necessary that the hairs be shaved over his head; then sign the limb where the abscess is, and then heat the cauterizer which is similar to a thorn, of which this is the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the cauterizer until the wound is healed, and it comes just to the skin, until the pus is all gone; after the cure according to the cure of wounds as long as they are clean; and it is not necessary that this cauterizer be used by anyone other than those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have never corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, it can be boldly attempted, and I believe that it is worthwhile to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	the fire cauterization
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should use the root of aristolochia for cauterization with fire, and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, the longest you can find, and dry it, and as thick and long as your finger; and crush it in oil, and take the cautery to the fire, and cauterize between the eyebrow and the collarbone, and two small cauteries a little down on the part that is outside the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the spine, declining a little behind; and one cautery in the middle, and one above the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the back, and one between the shoulders in front of the cautery that is between the shoulders. And do not press your hand, but do it openly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said that no man uses fire cauterization similar to the razor, and they scrape it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to the abscess; and then the pain is gone, as we have said in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear or the pain kills now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not improve, then they resort to three methods of cauterization that are good.
