Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the paper's shape returns according to what it should be, it is good; if not, take the razor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two cuts or at the angles of the incision that you have made, and make two angles so that when they are assembled, the shape is as if it were the shape of a letter that has not «I greek»; then remove that char, according to the quantity that its cost is away from, of what teaches the paper, then add the two missing parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then cure what we have said about softening medicines, and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the illness comes from a cut or stitch or cauterization, it is necessary to make a plain incision between the hairs of the skin, as I have said before; then squeeze between the two fingers of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters compare all possible means to see how it can return the figure to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for incision and instruments in many positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	soudement of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this sewing has been done by many people in a similar manner that the paper above is smeared with the white of oil, and cannot move or do its work naturally, then it is necessary to go outside the paper with the point of a razor, and lift it up; and extend it with pincers, until you scrape off what is hard at the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or too thin, so that the pain does not suffer that the spatula is too sharp or burns the oil; and let your incision, from which you scrape that assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and that whole assembly is healed, and nothing is ever done in strong vinegar, and lukewarm water, and collyrium; then place between the paper and the oil a linen cloth, and put above the oil soft wool in abundance; and after the injury use the collyrium and other remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways in which the elbow is affected: one is nervous and resembles a hard, painful knot, and another that is not nervous but resembles a frozen white moisture, so that when touched with iron and rubbed with pincers, it cannot be removed; and both begin near the great arm and grow slowly until they cover the whole eye and light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is such that the evil ones put their head in your hand, then the work begins with the eyes; and take the paper to your hand, then bend the elbow with pincers of small doubled, and raise it above; then take a needle, and put the hair of horse, or of cow, or of beef, and the thread strongly; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the elbow, and push the needle through all the needle, and tie the elbow with a thread and raise it above, and scrape all the hair on the side of the elbow that shows the pearl and the silk to the hair just below, then cover the remaining in the root of the arm to all the subtle spittle and with small forces, and leave the natural skin of the arm, so that by the incision the tears do not come out as usual; and once it was only the elbow at the end of the thread, and if the thread, as we have said; then scrape on all the soft tissue of which this is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be sure that the scalpel does not touch the gristle and break it, and that the water is not pierced; and after the incision pour a little broken silk thread into the oil, and a poultice made of litargire, and let it remain on the other side until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the joint is not flexible, and you cannot insert the needle, and the incisions cannot enter, often this appearance of a joint from medicines is cured; and they are born as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, then pour oil on the painful part, and take the scalpel lightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And rub the affected joint gently, and if you see that it does not soften and the pain is not relieved, then blow into the oil mixture made of litargire and red wine and beaten egg, and dampen the oil with the other hand; then continue the same work on the other affected joint until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is wrong with the oil, as if it causes an abscess to break, then milk it, and first cure the abscess until it is healed, then continue the work as before until it is completely healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm is night in the oil by great harm, then spread it on a cloth and let it sit for a part of the day and not all, until tears do not come; then pour red wine colloquium into the oil.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the meat that is born above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men are born without any red meat, and cover the pupil and hold it above papers and turn it back, and it looks like a balcony of balauste; and the work is that the hairs put their head in your own, then work the eyes, and all that meat has suitable incisions to this eye, and support it with force; then cover the first meat, and go all scraping to the razor just at the end, and make sure you do not scratch the oil in the work; and let the incision of the spatumile that we have said in the incision of the nail and as small forces of which one takes the base, as it forms after this chapter the demonstration; and when the incision is completed and all the meat is removed, then use the oil of silk broken or you distill red wine colloquium and similar corrosive medicines, and put on top of the oil cotton with abin of wool, so that it is assured of aposteme chaut; and if nothing remains, and the skin does not cover, and you doubt aposteme chaut, then leave the oil and treat the aposteme with things apaisant aposteme chaut; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do all meat that is treated in the oil by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in any case, it is necessary that you strengthen the care of each weakness of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes' veins
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	which are red veins that are covered over the oil, and take away from the sight their work and weaken the oil always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, the first thing you should look at is whether that oil has any other disease besides the red veins; then advise the patient as follows: command the evil that he puts his head in your clean place, then suspend those veins all around according to his wisdom, and let the circles be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two openings made gradually in one side of the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then apply gentle pressure to those openings gradually, and stop the bleeding with a bandage after some time, until you can remove those openings from the oil; and be careful not to pierce the oil with pointed spatulas, and do this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not stop until those openings are removed; and when you have done this, pour green and red wine into the oil to corrupt what remains behind.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all the blood in that hour, then apply a poultice over the oil of things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and let it remain for some time until the pain is relieved and it is ensured that an abscess has not formed, then resume according to this method as long as it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The master calls this "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cauterization and with medicine boiling as I have mentioned before, and it is not healed, then make an incision over the abscess where it must die, and drain all the pus that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the tooth is discovered, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then the instrument of all this is in its form; and it is called «sharp edge», and it must be made of iron from the chief, and it should not be pointed like a lime as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Then place the sharp edge above the jaw of the tooth, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is removed; and do this once, then restore the jaw with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the tooth is not sound, and there is no new growth, and the body of the gum is sound, and remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not again infected, and no bad accidents come, then it is healed; if not, then there is no other remedy than to return the abscess to the pus of the neck according to this form: and you must discover the tooth the second time by iron and by medicines, and when it is discovered take the foret according to this form, and let the chosen be of iron at three angles, and let the fust be attenuated just to the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it above the bone of the arm, and move your hand away from the oil I poc, then return to the whole forearm until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the pain as if it were coming from inside; and since you have restored the shoulder with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the char is born and hardens the bones, then apply the matter to the elbow; it is a lighter thing for the pain.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the end of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are wide open and do not waver, and there is no disturbance or drowsiness, then you must bind the pain; then cleanse it, then apply leeches or a heated iron to draw out the poison, then put on the oil with a mixture of acid, aloe, incense, and sarcocollis, and then strain the oil, and apply it with bandages and cloths; the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths that are soft enough, and double each one into four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need; then strain it through a sturdy cloth, and restart the leeches or heated iron to draw out the poison; then remove the leeches and let the oil remain strained day and night, and if it begins to recover, it is good; if not, then restart the bandages and cloths and the mixture and the leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	forced tearing of the uterus
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the uterus, it becomes open, and it is often covered with paper-like substances like resin, and it is difficult to see; if you see it covered, the work is such that you drive a needle into the root of the part below this, then drive another needle or double the thickness of the arm; and pierce it, and let the first needle follow its position; then bind the doubled thread around the uterus, and hold it tightly, then remove the needle and put oil on it with a lot of honey; and let it remain until the thread has healed with the uterus, then care for the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed; and the wound is never covered by the uterus from each part of a circular piece of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly swollen, pierce them with a thin needle that comes from the front of the oil, and drain the moisture and descend upon the eyelids, and enter immediately; then extract as much as they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the front of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than a drop that is assembled in the oil, resembling a sharp descending arrow, and this is not sharp; and the way of the appearance of the work is such that you make the pain sit on the seat prepared and straight, then take the chief between your hands for two parts, and move the muffler as much as you see the drop coming up to your eyes; then it should be fixed, and not descend and not be disassembled light, and see the things as they were; and if it does not descend, it is sharp, and if the descending drops are not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the painful part is placed between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it pass over the corneal thread and the conjunctive with the corone, until the bone is exposed; and when it is exposed, then pour hot, boiled oil mixed with honey, or vinegar or fenugreek root boiled with honey, then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have experienced similar things in the division, and what is needed to pierce; so work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary for you to seat the misaligned bone between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and with clean, tightly stretched oil; then place the oil-soaked cloth in your right hand if the bones are crossed, or in your left hand if they are not; then take in your right hand, if the bones are crossed, the instrument called «almagda», or in your left hand if they are not; then place the point of the «almagda» above the crown of the oil on the part of the elbow, then strike the «almagda» virtuously, and withdraw your hand until it pierces the crown of the oil, and feel that «almagda» is coming to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of «almagda» be at the front of the measure of the space between the sun and the beginning of the night; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cloth, and then place the instrument above it or at the sharp edge, then expressly remove one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if he sharpens it now, then he will see the hairs in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, and if he sharpens it again, the second time, put the thread with the instrument, and when it is well fixed and does not rise, gently turn around your hand slightly and slightly; then put a little bit of silk thread, and leave the eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by default the eye soaked or in minced meat and oil red and with enough fat, and tie with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	No, and those who are of our kind, put on top with enough fat.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the oil cannot enter due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you use the instrument called «albert», of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunctive, and do not go too far in front, but make the eye gentle, then drive out the hardness, as we have said; and at the completion of the work compare the patient with the sleep that comes, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark room; and for all movements, take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and tie him according to his disposition until the next day; then release him in the same dark room, and examine his sight, and make him see some things, and then return the bandage on the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this in the first hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you raise the eyelid, for the sharp pain quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, you should pour hot oil in front of the seventh hour, and apply what allays abscess; and when it is calmed, remove the cloth and put on its face a new one to cover any opening, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then slowly and gradually leave the house, and convert back to its usual state; and ensure that no one should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Some came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in some countries people do all kinds of things to succeed in archery, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read any in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of almsgiving, because those who do not know them see them; and they are made of pure tin properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the heads of them are of the same subtlety, and the rest in three angles downwards.
de la char sor le neis	of the chair for the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Noses never grow or are born different, because there are some that seem like scorpions at the end of the feet; and if there are such ones or they have a nose with a bad color, and if they have a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those noses that are good and not enhanced, it is necessary to place the bad between your hands against the sun; and work their nostrils, and pour the oil into those noses, and remove them; because it is appropriate that you can hold the subtle spike of one part, as long as you know that that nose is completely dry.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains nothing that can be covered, open it with all the subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if it is a boil, clean it as it should be; and if it is malignant boils, hurry and cauterize it until the wound is not moist and all the pus is removed. Then pour or rinse with cold and sharp wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the wound does not close, and moisture comes into the palate, if it does not pierce as it should, there is a bone above, preventing the instruments from cutting: therefore you must go with a piece of linen a little thick, and be careful of your hands, and leave a space between each thread of an inch or less; and put the bad ones on the thread of the linen into the wound to come out through the nose; and pull it out as far as it can go inside the mouth; and often do this with children at school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the one coming out through the nose with one hand, and the other coming out of the mouth with the other hand, and clean them one after the other as we do with our fingers.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you see that they have not corrupted that char, then remove the filth, soak the wound with blood, and moisten the cloth in Egyptian oil, and put it back on the nose as before; do this three times or more, until the ointment has corroded all that remains of the char; then put a plaster of unsalted butter for several days until it is healed, and if it needs medicated oils, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, by which one distills oils and medicines on the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a cup, and conduct it thus; and if you see, make a closed cup, and let the instruments be plain for purifying the head; and have one hand on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the fire cautery
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease arises at the tip of the nose that is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large, as if it were a separate thing to look at; and for this reason, it is necessary to cover it at the beginning, and let it all go, then place the fire cautery or the burning medicine on the tip of the nose; and if one delays in covering it until it is large, if it is hard, of poor color, and without sensation: if one does not touch it with iron, because it is an infected abscess, for when one covers it once, then great harm comes to the tip of the nose; and if the abscess is softly touched, not with iron, and you see that one can cover it all, then remove the disease and the covered part without fear, and cure the nose of other things that restrict and bind it.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut off and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	it is better to use one of these cartilaginous parts, which is more effective in some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, if the wound is fresh and full of blood, look at whether the lips are swollen on both sides; then stitch them together at a seam, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already scarred on one side and not on the other, it is necessary to scorch all the parts that are not healed, then bring the two lips together at a seam, bind them, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and broken incense; place the powders on a piece of strong or other strong plaster, and leave it until it bleeds through, then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is such that you assemble the wound: either by needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes there are abscesses inside the lips that are hard and resemble grains of different sizes, both small and large; therefore, it is necessary to turn out the lips, and cut under each one, and take the pus with forceps and clean every part; then apply the wound after incision with crushed garlic, until the pain is not stained; then the saliva, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the toothache
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	often arises above the teeth due to caries, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary to support it with forceps, and cover its root, and let out the pus or blood; then place on the tooth vitriol crushed glass, or other powders that are astringent and desiccating; and if the toothache returns after the incision, and often does, then cover it again, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Never gather the roots of teeth, within the mouth between the gums, sharp instruments that are disgusting and harsh; and never gather black, yellow, and green teeth, until corruption comes to the gum, and are foul-smelling; so you should make the bad thing between your hands, and its roots be in your holy place, and remove the roots or the sharp instruments that appear, until nothing remains; and thus make the black and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is at the first layer, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and be aware that teeth have a matter of various forms of instruments for removal, according to what the work demonstrates, because the razor that removes the teeth has other forms than those that remove between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat the toothache, do not delay in pulling it as long as possible, for no one should do this; for it is a substance very high and thus one does not have any excuse to pull it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the toothache is severe and you must pull it, then it is necessary to be sure of the tooth that hurts.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the toothache is due to an unholy tooth, and one must check if it is a holy tooth, and pull out the good tooth; and then the pain does not depart immediately, because the evil ones are still there, for we have already done this to these saints; and when you are sure of the tooth that hurts, then it is necessary to burn around the tooth on all sides very hard to protect the gum from all parts; then loosen it with your fingers or subtle pliers at the first and second joint, until it is well dislocated, then tighten the pliers well; and let the one who has the toothache in your holy mouth between your teeth, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump back, take any of these instruments and gently tap on each part lightly, and shake it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and damaged, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the pulp is; and if the extraction is subtly tied with wires, so that it does not break during extraction; and it is very important to cover around the gum to displace the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and that a part remains, and again cause pain by the evil of the root greater pains of the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be warned that you do not act in such a way as the ignorant physicians who, by their haste and boldness, break the chariots every time, and do not heal what we have told; but bring about once by the quackery of this great disease for the roots that they delay, or for the chariot that they break, as we often see; and when the dense is drawn, wash the limb with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood comes out, which often happens, use the limb with broken glass; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, by which one moves the first tooth, should be long and thick, so that they do not double back when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick-bodied so that they do not bend when pulling out the tooth, and they should be made of good iron, and they should be sharp to hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling out the tooth, it is necessary to put a piece of clean, soft cotton on the tooth or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	so that the tooth is worn down, then insert the pliers called "algefri," which the patient resembles a beak; and they should be made inside like a hook and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out at all these needles, then it is necessary that you dig around the root entirely, and put the tool called "althali", which is a spoon, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is too large and does not break in half, and if the root jumps upwards, it is good; if not, then you can use all the tools, of which these shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this tool with two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this tool which seems like large needles, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is not to be broken unless it cannot be repaired, and it is made of many dense materials; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned here; and the wise masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their work and the disease show them, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach about the instrument due to the diversity of the cases and if it is broken, since if they search for the instruments that are necessary, as I have told you and helped with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they are thick and well holding to hold the bone so it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; then restore the limb with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is pus in the bone and it is small, then the whole instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural course, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, it is necessary that you remove the tooth after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot be a dentist without it: then the rat; and if it is attached with the tooth, take this instrument which is shaped like a small beak, and it is similar to a sharp iron pointed at the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the hammer gently and slowly for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be extracted, then the lime from a piece of lime shaped like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the lime of which we make arrows; and in the lime, the tooth is gradually and gently moved, so that it does not move until it is cut; then the flat end is used to scrape away all the roughness, and if the teeth are too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth in front are loose, or by percussion or falling out, and the pain cannot press upwards because it makes them bleed, and you must treat them with tightening medicines, but this does not work; then you must tie them with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are moving, take the wire and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the broken teeth between the healthy ones, if there is one or more, until you feel secure on the other side; then start the covering again from the part where you began, and press your hand subtly and securely, so that it does not move at all; and let your wire be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the broken teeth with a thin wire, and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth and the gum, so that it does not bleed the tongue; and then leave it so tight as it can hold, and if it slips, or the wire breaks, if you have another wire, it holds and serves in this way throughout its length, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the cementing of two healthy teeth, and two broken ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth breaks, if you put it back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and it does not interfere with anything that is wise and suffering, and never made the shape of a bone tooth of a cow, and put it in the place where the defect is, and tie it as we have said, and holds and serves in this way throughout its length.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of covering the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There are no joints of the tongue that come out of its place or by nature, which is born thus; or by accident of a wound; and the works are such that you open the mouth of the painful, and hold their head in your own, and raise the tongue; then cover the nervous of the large, until the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or not, and it is from a severe wound, if you boil the thistle and cover the large gently; and be careful that the wound is not too much in front, for the artery which is out; and when you have done, lift the tongue of high rose and of cooling, or of high cold, then put out the tongue a linen tent; and the wound every night, so that the tongue cannot stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood comes out, put some borax on the wound; and if it does not stop bleeding, cauterize with slow-burning charcoal, which is good for the wound; then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is a black or dark and hard spot, where the patient does not feel pain, do not touch it, for it is chancre; and if it is declining towards discharge, and there is moisture, pour some thin alcohol on it from both sides, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if it does not stop bleeding at your work, put borax on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you have removed all of it; then lift the wound dressing and bandage, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No time comes from within the throat boils that are called "godath", and they are properly called the two tonsils, and when you cure them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if it is an abscess hard and of small size and of yellow color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, but let it drain as much blood as possible; and then you will break it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first check that the abscess has rested and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then place the misaligned limb in front of the sun, and its joint should be in a straight position, and the instrument should be held in one's hand, and press the tongue away from all the tools, from which this form is made; and it should be of silver or fine brass like some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue against all these tools, and you see the abscess, then take the lancet and the needle in the amber, and bring it up above as much as you can; and take nothing else with you, then cover the instrument, of which this form is made, which looks like a forceps; and all the while the head is bent, one side to the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use a pair of pliers, with which it has the following form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And on one side, it is sharp, and on the other, blunt; and when you have removed one of the tongs, remove the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the sharp pain with hot, sharp, and salty water, and if blood comes out, gargle the sharp pain with hot, squeezed juice of green pomegranates or mullet, and similar things, until the wound is clean; then cure it until it is healed; and never do other abscesses than the two tongs, so remove them in the same way as the two tongs should be.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	I treated a woman with an abscess that was lodged deep within her throat, namely a small abscess; it had nearly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe or swallow, and she died if she persisted in this condition for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had been punctured twice through the nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore immediately punctured it once through one nostril, then removed a large portion of the pus; I then punctured another part through the other nostril, and pressed on the tongue to keep the mouth open; after puncturing the abscess again, I removed a part, and only a small amount of blood came out; thus the woman was able to breathe again, and she began to drink water and wine, and did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; the abscess would recur and fill up the cavity that I had emptied, growing very large; therefore I pushed it back and cauterized it inside her throat: thus she did not grow worse; and I left her with these parts, and only God knows what happened to her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When referring to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, and you see that the abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then you should apply a poultice; and the one that is round and not long; and if it is bloody or dark red, then you should avoid incision of the.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in the pain.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	When you see it, as I have mentioned, according to its shortness and length, place the misaligned part in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the tool that we mentioned earlier; then make an incision at the one end, and remove it, and sew it with the two tools that I mentioned in the incision of the two needles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not sew more than the excess which is outside the natural limit; for if you sew too much, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we mentioned in the incision of the two needles, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is too great, then you should use a device for the cauterization of the sensitive area.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of the cauterization is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient places his head on your shoulder, and then presses his tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and applies it with very hot, quick fire, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and with this movement of the instrument, which is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the patient places his head on your shoulder, and then presses his tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and applies it with very hot, quick fire, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and with this movement of the instrument, which is the form: and places a hair or something on the medicine, like the movement of a spoon, and places the instrument on all the medicine over the tongue; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flows from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not drip down his throat and the blood; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it over the tongue for a quarter of an hour, until you see the medicine is working and the medicinal properties of the medicine are soothed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wipe the cotton in the medicine, and blow the instrument through the cotton into the throat, until the cotton is burned over the tongue; and do this often, until the cauterization of the medicine is perfect, then let it dry for four or five days; and if you have the skill to begin the cauterization of the medicine again, then begin, and after the cauterization wipe it around the tongue with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be washed with hot water, and be treated with garglings until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more safe from incision than the cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take sage and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and similar herbs, and gather all or some of them in a pot, and put vinegar in it, and let it boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the tips of the instruments should be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is dead; afterwards, repeat this often, until the eye dries, and guard that you do not make a hole at the beginning of the outbreak of the abscess, for many things happen; and do not make a hole except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a sponge and place it inside the mouth to prevent the patient from biting; for the sponge does not cause the steam to bother the mouth, and this is a good remedy together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often, one should pull out objects from the throat or fish bones, or nothing at all; therefore, you must remove what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun at all instruments, so that you can see the thing; and what does not open and is returned in the throat, it is necessary to make vomit the bad thing as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the thing is removed by vomiting; or the bad things swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or the small piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to the thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes back, it will be removed, and then pull out further; and if it does not come out because of what we have said, then take the instrument from the bottom according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instruments should be curved at the top so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that nothing enters it, or push the bone inside; and it is better that the hairs push the instrument, for it is often soft or the thing is as such; if the push goes down, or it pulls the entire instrument evenly, until it is full.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat's soreness
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No medicine is used for the throat's soreness, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and if it does not improve, then look at the throat's pain to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the shoulder blade, treat it with all small nails, or with delicate needles that are worth a lot.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not work, take a hairy cat, and put it in the neck of the patient, then pull out or move the hair of the cat with iron hot, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the wounds are infected all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in the direction of swallowing, and move it to his hand often; and when the shoulder blade soon feels the cold, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not die as we have said, then smoke the pain away with asafetida, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will disappear.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation is that you hold a pot with burning charcoal in it, and place it covered by a cloth perforated in the middle, and in which the smoke passes; then pour your fumigation, and put the head of the patient in his mouth, and close his mouth, so that the fumes do not escape but go up to his nose; and the nose will now clear up, and if it does not die, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient drink things that are salty and other, and do not drink anything sharp; and then he will be in a position where he can recover by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to treat the throat, namely when one can see it, resembles a curved hook to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a beak, and there is roughness from lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot slip.
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscess, according to what the memory comes here after one and another in this book, and they differ in puncture and cut; and it is in two ways that the one is in its own likeness, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for those who are at court.
