car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the shoulder are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if an abscess is not to be pierced until the boil is completely healed; and if for some it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beyond joints, and it is left until it is swollen around, perhaps because the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which it is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is located deep within the limb, and if you delay perforation until it has died, it will harm the main limb; or if it is located deep within the base, if you pierce it before it dies, it will not be able to pass through, and will remain long inside, and there comes a fistula; and it cannot be healed in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary to scrape the edge of the perforation of the abscess that has died according to completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and inflammation, and the relief and reduction of the main abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary to make the perforation where the abscess is most dependent, and where it opens most widely; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscesses are at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all cases equally where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the throat, it is better to leave the puncture until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before that, it may extend along the vein of the blood, and is covered in much filth; and perhaps they harden the lips and pierce through it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is punctured according to the wide vein, as the member has need of it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is appropriate to treat small abscesses with small incisions; and large abscesses with large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if such abscesses or it is necessary to cover them, and to dress them; when they have become as soft as cloth, and are softened, it is appropriate to treat them as one would with bubbles: and if such abscesses are cut in three angles, and if such abscesses are covered as the back of a mule, and other similar shapes, and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a boss, such as superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you puncture them clearly; and if the abscesses are large, and they have a lot of pus, and you puncture, if you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only a part; then treat the abscess on the other day, then take nothing else afterwards; do this gradually, many times, until the pus is all out; especially if the wounds are of weak virtue, or women carrying, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced ones, there is no need to fear with the end of the bow, for by chance, the patient may die, and you will not perish.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, dry the wound, and see if the abscess wound is small; and if a tailor complains, soothe him with linen or cotton cloth; and if there are large abscesses, and there is much pus, it is necessary that you fill each one with old cotton or shredded linen to avoid moisture, and tie it to the wound; then open, and treat the dressing until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding in your work, apply sharp cold and cooling, and wipe the cloth, and put it on the wound repeatedly for many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply proper treatment and care, and use the powders I mentioned in this book, and if it is very tense, and if the wound or abscess is very painful, then it is best to put on tents and wipes soaked in wine and oil; and if it is in a bad state, and the wound is charred, then it is best to use wipes soaked in cold and oil, or warm wine and oil, as we have said; and then remove the abscess, drain and treat, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	when small abscesses appear on the face, and are of the kind that are in cloth, such as the wart of a girl, and many are like this.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also large and such ones that have moisture like chickenpox; and if there are some that are hard and pustular at the cutting, and there is no doubt if the artery is not against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the belly are such that you test with all the tool called "rectoscope", from which the shape comes after, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then do it by passing through the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off nothing left behind that contains that moisture, for it returns when one leaves anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will continue what is remaining at night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, as before, the second day, and the third, until you are sure it will not remain overnight; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is large, then cut it open according to this form, from the long side; and pour in your medicines, and scrape the skin from all parts, and put all your care into drawing out the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for the abscess if it is pierced, and cut and treat as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And if the abscess is on the belly, it is less heavy, for it contains little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or boils has no moisture, and if it is one of the abscesses I copied from an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and could not break it; and if one had tried to cut it, they would have made as bad a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head or ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point of the ear, to let out the pus; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of tumors
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often have abscesses at the neck, and remove the tumors, and cause pain, and sometimes come from other parts or the chest, and are very large, and are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and each tumor is properly within its own side, as with the neck and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these tumors are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some evil ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that one which you see of good disposition in the touchwood, and is similar to the color of the chest, and moves from each part and is not attached to the neck or the artery or the conduit, and is not deeply rooted; then it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape off all parts, and stitch the two lips of the wound as we have said in abscesses of the head; and slowly and carefully, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and that it does not leave a spacious cavity or tear, which the hands cannot reach, and do not look too early, before you cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you pierce the vein or artery, and it does not let you open it, then put in the wound vitriol broth, or some powders that stop bleeding, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is healed, and then begin to poultice.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is clean, return to your work, until you complete it; then ask yourself if there are any small pustules remaining, and cut them and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a great vein in the root of the pustule, then it is only necessary to cut that pustule at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through, without causing harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire suppuration, it is necessary that you gather the two lips of the wound and hold them together, then since there is no excess due to the size of the suppuration.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you cover the root of it with a poultice and draw out the pus, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those suppurations that contain excess, pierce where it is most dead; and pierce in such a way as the one previously mentioned, hanging down, then apply bandages and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well covered, the cure of ointment encouraging char, until it is healthy.
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the throat-cutter; but I have never seen one in our land, and it is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the furrow of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and one should not help with this, because all the veins and the source of the evil are in those who have abscesses deeply in the mouth, or in the throat or in the lungs.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of choking.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary to cut it out in three circles or four with a small cut across, between the two circles or by the amount of the cut through the cartilage; and those are suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no char, and the vessel is long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary to stretch the skin of the neck all around, then cut the throat until it reaches the windpipe; avoid the veins of blood, if you see anything, and then cover the cartilage, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe that jumps through the limb that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed during which we doubt the strangulation, gather both lips of the wound together, and cover it completely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause blisters to rise until they are healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that we should not do this until the throat is completely stiffened, and the limbs are judged to be dead, and the defect has left.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, we cover the epiglottis because the limbs cannot remain, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and because they ordered the ancients to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease had passed, and it had passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew the wound and cure, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a dagger and put it in her throat, and cut part of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not bled much, the blood was coming out through the wound in the throat.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and bandaged the wound, and healed it until it was healed; and she did not die, only her voice was affected, and she returned to normal afterward; because I believe that in the tissue of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and is a large abscess in the color of a yolk, and is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; or naturally without a cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental way is in two ways: one resembles a large boil, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from us through an artery; and it has fear, and it does not require to be opened except by a small needle, and the proof and search are made throughout the entire puncture: if you find it as in a large boil, and cannot open any vein, then cover it as one would cover a large boil, and take it all at once, if there is none; and look for it quickly, and treat it as it should be, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	We have many ways, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to tell the difference between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that they are cold and feverish, until the boils have passed, and is accompanied by the purgation; then the fever and cold subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us, there is neither cold nor fever nor pain, and it contains the syphilitic pustule, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the skin, and begins like a small spot, and becomes large; and they are in two similarities, whether dry or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the care of a new patient, it is necessary to first test and examine them with an instrument called an "entromissoire", according to the form that follows in the chapter or treatise.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of examining abscesses among us is that you grasp or more moist skin than you pierce in the abscess, and turn your two fingers gently, until you feel that the instrument has reached the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the entromissoire, and be careful that it does not slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the wound is moist and has a certain color, make it so as I have said for the other abscesses; and if after the incision there is no more moisture, scrape off the fat, then cut it in a cross shape, and take pincers, and scrape lightly from every part and remove the skin where you think it is infected with the rot; and if you cannot remove it cleanly, tear it off in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, it returns many times; and if it lingers a little, and does not trouble you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, and close the wound, and put on things that soothe abscesses, and treat other treatments until it is healed; and if the wound is large, cut out both lips of the wound, and treat what remains with char.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if it is against you or another, if you are hurried and fill the wound with broken glass, let it remain for two or three days until the wound heals, and rest the exudation of blood; then return to the copper that was left behind.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See the forms of instruments used for extraction, and there are three ways: large and medium and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three ways: large, medium, and small, to extract the arrows from fistulas; and they are like the needles that one buys for sewing, and are made of brass, or iron, or silver, and are worth as much as those that are yellow, and are more effective for extracting splinters from fistulas; and they are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the wound.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the needles are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are needles with two barbs in three ways; and if there are needles with three barbs, and they are also of three ways; and if there are needles with two barbs, and a needle of one barb alone, and they are also of three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these that we make are sharp, and there are some that do not cut except from one part, so that we can peel the skin, because we do not cut the vein or the nerve; and these puncturing instruments are the needles returned in needles, so that the pain does not persist at the opening of the abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and never used is another tool small, resembling the scraper of pustules, according to this form, with which we drain blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is never put back in place that it should have been, and it does not heal the veins, and it does not heal according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as if they were breasts of a woman; and they remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them should follow this form of this line from b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with healing charcoal, then sew together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks down, and is softened because of its great size like in women, and if it is made into two pieces above, by similar cuts; so that one holds to the other at the end of each, so that the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line b to the line g; then scrape off the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitches and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the pain does not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then you should fill the wound with moistened corrosive cotton gauze; and let it remain until it removes the remaining fat and the fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of boils on the hips
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These boils that come from the hips are hard scrofula or have crusts, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the wound in the boil is emptied, apply old cotton to the wound and leave it there until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment as appropriate until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, then pierce them as we have said in puncturing scrofula, and if the wound remains open, then treat it with cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the bursting of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is burst and the skin above is bruised, then there are often abscesses, and also bleeding from the vein; and if one knows it is for the artery, then the abscess should be lanced longways; and when you feel it with your fingers, it is stretched; and when it is for the vein, it should be bled; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside of the bones and joints and neck and mouth of other wounds, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the fire cauterization, and the one who is in charge should also avoid it, and in the one who is swollen from arterial bleeding through the long skin; then open the belly as one would for an incision, and remove the artery until it is exposed; then insert a needle on the other side, and pierce it with another needle just as I showed you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not remove the thread that is between the two strands of an interweave until the wound is healed, and if the abscess is in the belly, it is necessary to stain the thread with what comes from the abscess on all the skin, then remove the needle from the thread that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and there should be two threads, so that you can pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I said, or the thread of one of the two parts of the needles at the incision of the first needle; and if you doubt that the thread will not hold, then take another needle all the way through the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four knots; then cover the abscess until the excess is gone, then cover the wound and leave what is tied; then put a piece of moist cloth on wine and oil, then treat the wounds and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and the vein, abscesses also come to the neck when they are cut, or from too much hard work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And they often come to the helpers and the doors in all of them where there are joints, and that is very painful, and its color looks like the color of the blood, and it is in many positions with pain; and when it is extracted, if it pricks, and it is not in front of the skin, but outside the skin; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor up or down, and those who are in joints do not usually cover them with iron: perhaps they contract; and those who are at the head or at the front, making the skin to the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if it has a point to a needle, and cut at its root; and if it is large, if it is suspended from the edge, and scrape, then bone, and stitch the wound at the seam, and cure until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never occurs in the belly and no other part of the body, and is a disease called "funge" by its resemblance to fungi, and has subtle roots, and large heads; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw the man who had two or belly that were more like funges than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were always moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one weighing eighteen ounces, and in the other six ounces, and the works in the incision is that you look if the hairs are moist, and the color of the arrowhead is white and moist and of subtle root; if the copper is large, and they are in your presence the fire cauterization.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting often comes many great corruptions of blood, and if you see the hair extending and painful from the incision of the iron, then take the thread well made, and tie the arrow as we have said, and leave it two days; then restrain, and do not cease to stretch the thread through the arrow until it reaches the arrowhead, and cut through it with work; and if the roots are large, then pour boiling water directly onto the belly, but you put well boil the half, then cauterize that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cover the thread which is of pale color and poor sense and of little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is a swelling abscess, and I will come to treat chancres afterward.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is bleeding heavily.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the wound is due to cauterization of a cut or puncture by a syringe, and it is above the belly and among some of the bruises, as in other wounds, or from blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is in front, or from vomiting; and if it is due to the tearing of the syringe and the exit of the pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various sources.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the end of the intestine, then it is most diverse, and when one presses it to its two ends, it returns, and perhaps it is torn, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when one presses it with their hand, do not force too much; and if it is due to blood, it is open by these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is filled with a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that one must look to see if it is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must let go of the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bladder, then you must command the patient to color his linen, and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the bed; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the limb that you have marked with a wide bandage, then stretch half of the abscess above the large muscle; then tie it around with a strong silk cord firmly, and let the intestine be loose; if you find the linen, then loosen it, and bring out the intestine from behind the belly; and if you find the bladder, then take it at the neck, and cut off the excess; and if the artery makes you contrary, or the vein, then go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and bring out two threads, and pierce the abscess with the two needles as you have done in cross that you will make percerate; then stretch the abscess into four parts above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the limb until it can bear weight, and cut off the dead flesh by itself; or you cover it when it has become thin and rotten, then cure what is necessary, and heal the abscess as we have said; and strain the blood or the moisture that you have taken, then cure the limb as it is necessary, and soak the limb.
dou chancre	The first sentence "Dou chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	In the division of chapters, we have described the resemblance of chancre and how to treat it with medicines, and how to use iron in the cure. And we say that chancre is more dangerous when it is in the mouth or where it can be easily removed like chancre in the breasts, in the throat, and similar places. It should be completely removed at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not advisable to approach it, for I have never seen anyone heal from it; nor has anyone ever been healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the work is in place where it can be removed, as we have said, you should once purge the pain of black bile; then if he has manifest repletion, bleed him, then wipe the pain from good bone to do the work; then pour your instruments or chancres, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow fully, and wipe well the place with your hand or something, and if the blood flows contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, if it cauterizes so that the wound is not stained; then cure other cures until he is healthy.
de ydropisie	de droguegie
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	In the division of hydropsy, we have mentioned the resemblances of dropsy, and how the assembly of the acute is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the treatment by medicines, and that which is treated by iron: if it is only eclites; and one should not touch with iron in these two resemblances: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarche, for it is a deadly thing; therefore, when you treat this resemblance of hydropsy which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the treatment does not work, if you look at whether the pain is weak, or if he has another disease besides hydropsy, as vomiting and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has no other disease but hydropsy alone, and he is not too young nor too old, then thus: gently raise the pain straight over your hands, and the ministers press the belly by bringing the acute to the lowest part of the least, then take the spatula in the shape of this:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And cutting of two parts, to the point, and ensure that no part is so thin that it can reach the intestines when thrown, and it cannot be bleached; then check if there is hydrops near the intestines: if necessary, cut off the third rib three inches from the spine on the right side; and if it is for the disease of the liver, then the incision should be on the left side of the third rib; and if it is for the gallbladder, then it should be on the right side, and it is not necessary that the hairs grow over the incision so that the excess does not run to the weakest liver; then cut through the skin with the instrument, and close it, and remove your hand from all the space between the skin and the gallbladder as if you were scraping at the quantity of an angle or around; then cut the gallbladder until the space reaches the desired length, and that is the edges of the wound, then remove this instrument with this form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of light rain or iron, and has in its part below a small puncture; and on one side, three punctures; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and it is cut as if by a pen, and this is the form of the incision that the scribes make to cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. de l’estopement de la verge	of the removal of the staff
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever born who does not have a wart on the staff, or the wart is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to prick quickly, do not pierce at all points very thinly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place or pierce the thin cloth of the bottom, and tie it and tie him in this way for three hours or four, and when he wants to urinate, if possible, remove the cloth, let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not convenient, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those who are pierced with small holes, if they are treated with a thin cloth of the bottom, as we have said, it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the piercing in their leg are blinded, for no one is born with the piercing at the top of the penis, because it cannot urinate before its penis rises; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the marsh, and it is a very bad disease.

And the manner of the work is such that the hairs lie so that the pain lies on its back, and the head of the rod and the copper are like the width of a pen, so that the puncture is made in the middle, as it should be; and beware of the blood that often comes, and if it does, use the bandage that stops bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often come boils in the rod, and it is an ugly appearance; and there are both good and bad ones; if it is necessary to prick them with a thin needle, and cover and clean all of them, then put on moist cotton in Egyptian oil; then treat the ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is malignant, of putrid color and fetid, then it is necessary to cauterize with fire.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood comes out, then apply the lunar cauterization according to this form:

The cauterizer is helpful in two positions: when blood comes out and when there is corruption; and if the tip of the rod is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to apply a piece of cloth soaked in piss on the wounds and urinate on them; and when the flesh is pulled out to the head of the rod which has not been circumcised before, or if it is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to scorch it with the instrument until the sinews are loosened, and deliver the patient from the rod in all parts; and if this is a difficult matter to decide, then it is necessary to scorch it at the head of the rod and the skin, and then apply a thin layer of linen cloth soaked in cold water, so that it does not come out again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not one of the minor wounds like the others; however, when we perform this work by our own will, and properly with children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least harmful to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not perform circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision in that time, and they all did it in one go; if it was lucky, there were two threads, and by chance if the thread on top and below detained the other, it would not hold.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	For the recovery, it is double the pain, and the wound healing is not always assured at the tip of the member; and the healing of the angle by chance escapes the iron, and corrupts the work, and often they are born in such a way that they have no need of healing and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the healing that is done by force to all the length of the thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in all the length of the thread; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and that the way of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he listens, that you only bind the thread around the rod as much as possible, and then throw it in all ways that you can; then put your hand straight on the rod, and gather the forces between your hands or outside your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then close your hand around the rod and blow gently, and take it up high until the part of the rod is clean; then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it outside one to the other limb; and keep it as two by the second work to the pouch and to the docket index, and cover between the two limbs, then lift the gently and take the head of the rod; then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the most dangerous; and put powder on top and on top of the powder a poultice made of a piece of rag cooked in hasty pudding mixed with rose water, boiled with red wine and fresh, and leave it there until the other day, and the cure of another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the mutilation is as follows: both shoulders are tense and are stretched, and they are the same as the other hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mutilation is when the knife goes inside the incision; therefore, it is necessary to extend it to your finger, in the same way that the other hand makes an abscess; and the copper equally, and if you cannot hold it to your finger, then hold it with tongs, and then the copper.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass for three days, and what is outside the rod is swollen, let it remain until the abscess is healed, and scrape lightly; and if the copper can be moved, and you keep away from the part of the rod, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez. dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or blood frozen, or bowel, or a charred, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention by the stone which is high or col of the bladder, then it is necessary that the pain soaks up its knees; and its feet are put on the back, and its belly is stretched from the part above the back, and it restrains the pain as much as it can; and therefore the neck of the bladder is pressed above the stone, because the urine is released and; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the pain is great, then you must administer extraction to all the instrument which is called «siringue», of which this is the form: and it is made of thin silver hair, like the pen of an owl; and it is made of a palm length and a half, and subtle at the head.
