And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the thread to the top of the linen or cotton pouch, and pull the head of the thread through the sling; and cover the excess of the linen and pull it up to the head of the sling, then oil the sling with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a chair, and the urethra and the wet cloth of oil and olive oil and vinegar; then press the sling heavily on the urethra until it reaches the root of the urethra, then double the urethra upwards over the cloth; then pull the sling forward just above the cloth, and the patient feels the urine coming just above the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order except that the conductor or it goes twisted; then tie the thread at each end of the pouch and the urine follows the pouch, then remove it, and correct the urine; and repeat the sling until the bladder is empty and aligned with the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When skin or blood comes into the bladder, and putrefaction is present, and you see it distill acidic and medicinal substances, then use all the instrument called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads are passed through it so that the medicine can penetrate well to the end of the catheter, so that the moisture can be drawn out and put where necessary; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, place the head of the syringe in the moisture, and draw from the drawing which is on the side; then draw the moisture into the syringe, and squeeze it strongly back onto the side; then the moisture will enter the syringe, and come to the bladder now, so that the painful sensations will be felt. And this is the form of the subtle catheter with which one catheters the bladder: if it is thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of archil, and is the highest of the two; and it is removed from the side where the joints are located; then take a bladder of sheep and put the moisture that you saw to cluster the bladder, then place it between the two breasts formed by a good double thread, and heat the poultice over the fire; then pour the head of the poultice into the stick, then hold your hand on the bladder with all the moisture evenly, until the hairs feel that that moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then pull the thread strongly in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dal, and put inside what you saw oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone, and extraction together with remedies; and I have said the difference between the arrow embedded in the rain, and all the signs, and in which stone one should open a hole; and in the bladder, and in the stick; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the arrow embedded in the bladder occurs more often in children, and it is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder resembles sharp pain in its subtlety; and if one opens it, there is great pain and much bleeding, and it can happen many times, and then it returns; and at most of these pains, the foundations; and it is light for the healing of children up to the age of four, and it is very grievous in old people, and is constant in those who are between young and old; and it is a lighter cure for those who have the arrow large, than for those who have it small.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with chalk, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders one from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and stand it upright and move it away from the body, so that the stone descends to the edge of the feces, and never once rises above the thigh; then place it between your hands and clean it, and your hands should be away from the thighs, so that the feces is entirely declining downwards; then take it out and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut across the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not cry out at the slightest touch, then moisten your right index finger with oil from your right hand, if the pain is sharp, or your middle finger, if the pain is dull; and press it into her foundation, and cut into the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then apply it to the neck of the bladder; then press upwards, and cut away where you see it tailor-made.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the midwife to press the bladder with her hand, and command her to extend her right hand to the uterus above, and her left hand to remove the skin that is outside the uterus in the part where the incision is made; then cut the spatula-shaped, from which it is formed:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And making an incision between what is between the ribs and the foundation, not in the middle but on the right side of the naval; and let it be straight above the stone, and your knife at the foundation or the bottom, and let it be like a slit that is wide by default, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure of the knife that is at the foundation, that it would jump out without effort; and if there is a stone where it is at the foundation, let it be sharp to cut out; and if there is a part that is soft, like a glass, and rounded, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	When there are angles and margins where it is, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump, then it is necessary to strain it with nails that are as thick as a lime at the head, to prevent the stone from escaping; or you can use a subtle hook bent at the head; and if you cannot engage it in this way, then enlarge the opening slightly, and if there is no decortication, then strain it with vinegar; and if there are more than one stone, then first remove the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove the small ones afterward if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If it is very large, then it must be cut larger, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the wound: either it dies, or the urine comes out through the place where the wound cannot heal; but all the while you try to draw, or to tear with pincers, until you tear it into pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put a moist cloth on top of the oil and wine, or oil and vinegar and cold vinegar, to soothe the abscess; then re-sew the wound on its own side, and do not remove the bandage until the next day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, the joint of oil and vinegar rises very well, then treat with ointment and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by the urine, which is known in a similar way as without any urine: then put your hand on the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, it will rot the bladder, and damage it; then lift the wound with vinegar and salt and oil, and help it in all ways that you can, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the remedies that you cure it with, that you tie the two thighs, and gather the medicines above the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the arrow is small and it is conducted with a stick, and tied up, and the urine cannot come out; then the cure that I have said before, that you cut many times, is to excuse the cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this already.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron in this form and be at three angles tied up in one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie the arrow around the stick outside of the bladder, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then lightly beat the iron on the stick until it reaches the arrow; and gradually turn the iron in your hand on the arrow until you can pierce the arrow from the other side; if the urine comes out immediately, then press your hand above where the part that is remaining inside the stick.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is currently broken, and has sprung with the urine, and is sharp to the limbs; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then tie a thread below the stone and the other above, then make the rod in the right place between the two threads, then pull it out, and release the thread, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound; and cure until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is rarely any stone in women, and if it ever occurs, the cure is difficult, and is prohibited for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well versed who will expose herself to shame, specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that if the woman's stone is more forward than the man's, because it should be cut deeper, and there is great pain involved. And if necessary, you should send for a woman who is well-skilled, and point out to her what to do, and if you cannot find one, then you must perform the operation yourself with great subtility; and present a clean needle in the vagina of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command during the examination of the stone; and look very closely to see if the woman is virgin: therefore, it is necessary to put on gloves and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she must push it out of her body, and recommend that she push it out or with pain, and press her right hand firmly against the vagina.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she move it from great to great from the entrance of the anus until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle part where it is muddy and stained, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her arm above the stone or away from it, and let the tailor make a small opening in the belly, if you feel the stone so sharp that the wound can be opened as soon as the stone can be removed, and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small and large and sharp and smooth, long and round and with rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you recognize the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if you do not know, put the similar stone in vinegar for an hour until the pain is gone; then return to your work, until the stone is softened, and have the tools that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone for you to help in your work; and if you do not know, and it is the artery that is cut, put powder on the wound and bandages and bendles, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest by chance the patient die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound has healed, return to your work, until the stone is fully formed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia cause
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than the assembly of moisture or white smegma, which is outside the foreskin, which contains the urine; and it is called "smegma", and never properly in the skin of the other urethra, if one cares that it is not there.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this smegma is due to weakness that comes from the foreskin, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes if it comes from percussion on the ribs, and this moisture has many colors: whether it is declining to yellow, or without red, or black, or aquous white, and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, because if it is white and facial as we have said, then it is the abscesses that we have mentioned, and if it is short and does not open the ribs, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own cloth, then it is the abscesses that we have mentioned with a part of the egg, and because one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the ribs and the white facial, then it feels bad; therefore when you see the color of the moisture, try all the previous forms.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introduction, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary to clean the hairs according to the power and the replacement of its body; then place it on its back, on something slightly elevated, and cover it with much cloth; then bend over its right side, and command the minister to bend over its left, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the sternum; then take the spatula and scrape the skin of the ribs from long to above the knuckle, and let your cut be straight in dividing the skin of the ribs up to the white face, and scrape the thin skin according to the power; then pierce the white plain with a sharp and wide cut, and extract all the sharpness, and then put your forceps, and press the white face above; and do not touch the sternum, but only the white face; scrape all or in pieces carefully the ribs of it subtly, if you do not scrape it well, it will return to the sharpness; and if the broken bone jumps to your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white face; then gather the two flaps of the sternum to one seam, then treat it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you trust the broken bone has been corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then cut off the coagulum from all the suspended parts, and extract the bone, and treat it as we have said.

And in all ways that you can, until you have removed everything; and be careful that the knife does not touch the bone; and cleanse this work so that it is safer; and guard against bleeding from the wounds, and guard against the work of the saw; and if nothing goes against you, such as an abscess or bleeding or other thing, then cure what goes against you according to what has been said before.

de l’aposteme des coions	of abscesses of the kidneys
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	In the section of this branch, there are many positions that cause fear in many people, which seems to me to be better left alone; and I will tell you about the work and similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come from the kidneys and immediately to the kidneys; and this is due to many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by excessive acid and ague, which is spread to the kidneys or from impact; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the blood; and there is no pain, and it is a severe abscess; and perhaps some gray and yellow abscesses, and of pus color, and never comes from an artery or vein inflammation.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the high placement of an abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it should only be touched there.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of opening a vein are known by their placement at the gentle touch of the fingers, and can often make the incision above this resemblance, and on other parts; and it is that you should care for the cures of the wounds, then the eye is raised high, and the thread from the white surface, and deliver the suspended part from all parts of the eye.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is already filled with these threads, then it should be incised, and the wound cared for; and if it is under the skin, or in the fluid within the vessels, then it should be completely removed, and the wound rounded properly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the shoulder blade is dislocated at its back, it is necessary that you cover it all, and straighten the neck, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your surgeries are completed, apply the wound with soft linen cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then use other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a kind of abscess enclosed in an envelope similar to a bursa, with the softening of the groin, and the painful movement of the limbs; and the treatment of this disease is as difficult as the previous one, and therefore we will tell you about its surgery, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to make the dislocated part sit on the seat raised high, then lift the suspensory ligament of the tendons down to your fingers, and all the veins that are close to the thigh, and scrape the masters, and extend them properly; then cut with a sharp knife across the wide part of the veins, as much as they are uncovered, and then scrape from every part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in temples; then take an needle or double-threaded needle, and tie it to the first limb where the blood came from, and tie it at the other end; then place them straight in the middle of the body, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as the others are treated with ointment, so that none of the veins become inflamed; for by this no harm comes, and if all the veins come out, it is necessary to pull the veins from all the limbs; so that the patient does not lose his circulation due to the incision of the veins, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this branch are from the section that comes out or from the extension over the belly in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from that toothache to one of the kidneys; and this toothache is either from the section or from the extension of it, and these two methods come from many causes: from shock, from jumping, from noise, or from lifting heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the toothache, are that it is painful and painful in a long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is equal to the kidneys towards the front, because the toothache approaches the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to the cutting of the abscess, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and has various apparances outside the skin, and is for the end of the intestine and the heart because of the cutting of the abscess.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are torn with the wounds, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer in the abdomen, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cases of iron, because it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way of the work is that you command or make the patient roll up the intestines with their hand inside the wound, if they can push them in; then place the neck above and between your hands, and release the fingers; then put the chest above, and cover all the skin of the belly with oil; then drive out the pus that has collected under the white skin that is outside the belly skin, until all the pus can come out; then scrape the abscess that is outside the belly skin, so that all the white skin is removed from all parts; then drive out your index finger in the direction of the belly, between the white skin that is outside the belly skin and between the second white skin, and behind the belly, and between the second white skin; and move the abscess with your left hand inside the belly skin, and place the white skin in your right hand above, and release the belly from all over the lower part of the belly; and command the assistant to stretch the belly up, and remove everything that is behind the bandage; and if you find anything, drive it into the belly through the back; then take a needle or a thick thread made of twelve strands of wool, and drive it into the back part of the abscess, which is outside the belly skin; then cover the threads with oil, and tie them together in the shape of a cross, and tie the abscess, which is outside the belly skin, with a strong thread of two strands; then cover the threads with oil, and tie them together in two strands, so that none of the wool that grows can enter into openings, that an abscess does not form; and finally tie the first thread according to the first thread, and leave the great thread which is outside the belly skin the length of one finger; and then the other according to the round shape that the belly has; then cover the part that is outside the belly skin with oil, and the bandage, as we have said before; then apply a soft cloth soaked in oil to the wounds, and apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white pustule that we have mentioned after incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this has often happened, and let the wound remain until it heals through it; and if it takes too long to settle, then apply hot vinegar on top of what we have said, until it heals; then treat the wound with other treatments, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made as the branch that is together with the viscera, in a similar way that you tie the vessels, after the incision lightly above; then cover over, and treat the abscess with what works, until the vessels heal; and the cure as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No tearing or anger ever comes, as we have said, and open the wounds; and let no one pull out any of the intestines with their fingers, and if they do, it is little, and repair every hour; and in any case, if it remains too long at this point, the wound or the syphac believes that the intestine is pulling out; and this happens by the extension of the syphac which is at the tears, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is softened and inflated the wounds and open; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have said before; and in this way no cure is done: and it is that the pains are squeezed between his back between your hands, then cover the tear enflamed according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the syphac which is outside the skin that the skin is on, then take the right and put it on the wound of the syphac; and press on the front of the belly, then cut the two wounds according to the syphac on the head of the right, and both; then extract the head of the right, and do not cover the syphac or extend the belly or other things, as I have told you in the cure of the intestines; then cure by the cure of the wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the hair, if it is damaged, heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The wound is constricted, and does not appear to be ruptured, and the cauterization is quiet in this place, and more proximal to the healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the boots
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the leather of the boots is softened in some men, because the char inside is softened, and it can be seen; and it is important, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the wound lie on its back, and cut the softened leather above the natural leather; then bring the two edges together at a seam, and if you see, first remove the excess of the softened leather at three or four stitches firmly; then sew between the seams, and cure it like other wounds until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	with great care
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	It is commendable to act with great care in our law, and for this reason I would like that I not speak of it much in this book; and it is necessary only for two ways: the one is that the patient responds truthfully when asked, and to cure with great care; and the other, because we often have need of careful handling of some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and rabbits and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that careful handling is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, make the animal sit in high heat, until the sinews are softened and held; then take them in your hand, until they are returned and you do not feel them anymore.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the treatment of hip: it is necessary to apply the beast, and press the skin of the thighs with your right hand, then tie the suspensory, and cop over each bone at the top, when you have well burned them; and leave no pus or subtle pus that is on the bones; and this method of treatment is more effective than that made by attraction, because by attraction something from the thighs remains, by which the beast desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	For the treatment of hermaphrodites:
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite is in two ways as men: one is that between the two thighs open as the shape of a woman according to nature, and sometimes they have hair, and sometimes they do not urinate.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And in women, it is done by placing a finger under the nipple as if holding a wand and two fingers above.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the care of the mouth and the female parts is that you remove all infected tissues and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine sprays from the skin of the penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tenting is an infected tissue above the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to clean the excess of the tentigenous matter from your hand or fingers, and wipe it lightly; and not alter much too soon, because blood does not come immediately, then cure other cures until they are healed; and in another char that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and use it, and by chance it jumps up, and it is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this reason they called the old "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to clean it as we have said the tentigenous matter, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of a woman is not clearly perceived, or the cause is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come to her; or it is due to charm applied, or subtle, sharp, or clever, and it is made from within the marriage, or the cost, or outside, or whatever; and they prevent conception, and pregnancy, and possibly the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the look of the body.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the symptoms are close at hand, then you should do it yourself or ask someone else.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a delicate and subtle case, and it is close to the two thighs, then hurry, and do as follows: bring your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two thighs, until the delicate and subtle case is removed, and is over the stomach; then take linen, and moisten it in oil, and place it on the leg, and grind the woman against a hard surface every day, so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the case is hard and sharp, it is necessary to use a copper spoon similar to a leaf of mint.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from a charred wound, if it is lifted and covered with a cloth; and have the medicines to stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, and abundant amount of honey; then apply a large piece of clean cloth, so that the wound does not stick together; and thus it should be long, and cover it with a tent of dry linen; then treat other cures until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh there is a charred wound, if it should be covered like this, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is in the marsh, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually bleed, and when hemorrhoids become old, they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and thrombosed veins, when they are present in the marsh, and do not appear until felt, are treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that can be felt at the edge of the marsh are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, it is necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the thrombosed vein with pincers, and cut off its root, then powder with restricting medicines such as acacia and sulfur and incense, and similar things; then boil her feet for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if there is any blood that comes out, sit her in a decoction of sumac and peel of green pomes and gall nuts and similar things, and then take wheat flour, and mix with honey and egg, and make an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he is stiff, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping glasses to his back and breasts without causing harm; then take the limb, and moisten it with juice of plantain or of aglanthe mixed with old wine, and apply to the joint.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, treat the limb with poultices until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a harsh sore, if you cover it as I have said for thistle; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscess come in the marsh, such as chancre and pustular abscess and herpes and esthenomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and chronic abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the chapter.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary to tell in this treatment of the chronic abscess that comes in the marsh, which is not one of the abscesses that come quickly; and if you know how to use iron, look at the abscess to see if it is red at the beginning of its appearance, and if it has fever and chills, and if it becomes red.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce, but make him wait until the pain is eased; then place the misaligned part on a seat, and have two small seats where he leans, and support it on its back and gather its feet to the sides of the leg; and let his knees be spread, and put his arms away from his hips, and tie them well with a good belt; then bring him the spatula used to open the mouth of the marsh, from which afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see this tool being applied, you check the depth of the marsh, so that what enters into the tool does not go further than it should, and that it does not injure the misaligned part; and if the tool is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marsh with cloths, so that the tool does not hurt it; and it is necessary for him to put the horn of the tool on top, and stain the tool.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is done by hand, if it needs to be covered at the head, cover it with a sponge soaked in rose oil or dry green oil; and place the tent of the wound at the front of the marsh, and place above the marsh and above the other clean moist cloth boiled in hot water or vinegar; then after two hours of boiling, when the patient is healed, continue boiling until they are healed; and never raise the marsh and the wound by a poultice of hot water and honey, and then with hot water or roots of lilies and aristolochia long soaked, then reapply the boiling.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set in the marsh, it is necessary that you guard against cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The midwife is first to the bed when she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see the woman approaching, and desires to smell the ar: then hasten the child to issue; then scrape that childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the second with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly his belly, so that the child issues quickly; for when it goes over its head, the second is with it, and is drowned in the marsh of its superfluities by good cleaning; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes up from its feet, and comes up the back or the shoulder, and the hands, or it comes up over its belly, or sometimes, and is turned over on its own collar, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the bailiff that she be wise and subtle in these things, and if she is deceived and disappointed, and I will show you all the figures how to help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes up through its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth with great pain, and her strength is weak, then let the midwife sit on a seat, or let the women hold her; and apply to her nature oil of olive or fenugreek cooked, and then give the midwife between her two little fingers the smallest spatula of which there is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and pierce the second joint, and hold it at its angle until the moisture that is inside has been removed; and take the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not, then you must apply a cataplasm of fenugreek with sesame oil to the woman's genitals; then let her chew and spit out the mixture for an hour: if this is now effective, the child will be born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If both hands are dislocated, it is necessary to reset them very gently; and if they cannot be put back in place, then you must make the woman sit on a chair, and raise her legs up; then remove the chair from under her, and wipe the woman, so that she does not faint at the raising; and if the hands still cannot be put back in place, and the child has died, then you must reset them at the hip joint which was previously dislocated, and extract the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, it is necessary to put it up high; then turn it gently and gradually, until it is level; then grasp both feet and extend them gently and gradually.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up suddenly, command it to hold still, and make it spit out the contents of its mouth; if it jumps far, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, turn it gently and gradually, until it is in the natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it is completely straight.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take muscle powder from high altitude, and oil of sage, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside of this ointment, then make her sit in high temperature until just outside the ribs; and when she is softened outside, make her a collar of mustard, and put it on, and let it stay for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child is born now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, place your hands gently and gently; then lean it on its neck, and hang its feet down, and lie it on the bed; gently fold your hands, and then grasp its hands on its belly, and remove the blankets from it, until it is clean below; and if the child does not cry, take its feet and gently move them, then gently move its belly upwards, then close your hands; and feed the child gently; and command the woman to hold it until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out wide a hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to engineer to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, lift the woman, and go; if she cannot go, then lie her on the bed, and bend her legs; then alleviate the muscle that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then sit her on a chair, then study to bring back the hand; and when the child is according to the natural figure, and make it suckle, and command that she breastfeed until the child is full.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and it has spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother's
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the patient to wash their hand, then turn it back and forth gently; and when it is even, if there is a muscular spasm of high and oil, as we have said, then command her to move slowly; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to hold it tight; and make her spit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way, for all the other fingers.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to doing this with all the other fingers, if the second finger can be bent at your angle, as long as the moisture is drained; and if it is stuck upwards towards its face and neck, then bend it downwards, so that it is not held, and break the bone; then push the child inwards, until you have put it back in place, and command the woman to hold it tight: then gently move it.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the discharge of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is often the case that twins are born, and sometimes they are born three or four at a time; and this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is an uncommon thing, and they do not live long, unless they are multiplied; I know that they are devised by the syphilitic disease, which is joined to the womb; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one at a time, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born gently, as the cure as we have said, and if the placenta is subtle, and it does what it does quickly and lightly; and do so that it is worthwhile for health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	None of them are formed in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, or more than fifteen years, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise doctor, and it is fitting that the bailiff should know all this, because by chance similar things may happen; so do according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When caring for the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and if nothing comes out, and you are forced to handwork; it is fitting that you should know whether the woman is of healthy virtue and has no accident or fear of death; it is fitting that the woman be laid on her back, and her arms inclined downwards, and her legs raised; then the midwife applies two fingers, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not treated with the extraction of the child; then rub the mouth of the woman with moist oils and mustard and seeds of linseed, then the midwife applies her hands to these oils and mustard; then she lightly inserts them into the woman's mouth, then if she swallows the fingers that are convenient for her, and if the child is discharged above its head; if she does not discharge it, then insert the fingers in her eyes or on her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or behind the beard or on the chin or on the sides, and if the child discharges above its feet, then apply it to the chest or the back; it is fitting that she ties the finger to her right hand, and places the tube between her left hand's fingers, and she squeezes all her hand lightly, and inserts the finger in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another bone, where the joint is located, so that the extraction is equal; and then place it equally by moving from one side to the other, to make it move, and hold the bones together as follows:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, apply some of its oil to the affected area, and push it into that part, and remove the other part; and if none remains, place this bone or higher up the limb, and keep moving until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by the pressure, then you must wrap it around the injured part until it all comes out; then place it in the joint of the foot or the elbow, and so you must do in the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	If the head of the child is large and it is difficult to extract at birth, or if the neck is too stiff, it is necessary to use a hook-shaped instrument between your fingers, and by pulling the neck and straightening it; or you can use an instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one; and thus the same thing should be done in the case of a child born with a natural curvature of the neck; and then remove the bones with pliers, and if the head is stuck, it should be forced out with forceps, until the blood that has issued is stopped; and if it cannot be extracted, it should be cut off in pieces as much as possible; and if it is inflated in the belly or outside the ribs, it is necessary to pierce it until the blood flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	If it is hanging above its feet, then it is lightly pulled, and the marrow at the base of the tongue is also light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is stiff in the belly or the groin, it is recommended that you pull it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and when the belly or groin is opened, remove all the moisture until there is none left; and if other members are also broken, and the patient remains conscious, then hold his hand in front of the tongue, and pull it back to the mouth of the tongue; then bite down once or twice, and then pull it out; and if the mouth of the tongue is retracted due to an abscess that has formed, do not force it, but instead administer moist and greasy things; and apply wet and soothing dressings, and keep them in a cool, softening, and moistening state.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the shoulder is dislocated above its place, and you can put it back in place, as we have mentioned in the living child; and if there is no way to do so, then break the bone and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, as we have mentioned in the abscesses that come in the marsh; and if blood comes out, it should be applied with high pressure, and other treatments should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, then consulted the other with this one, and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses formed in the throat, and they swelled so much that they burst, and began to cause great pain.
