je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to the doctor, and he thought for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong adhesive, and some bones stuck to it, and after a while, others did as well.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised, because the belly does not have bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and in it were many bones, until the woman was better; and the woman thought for a long time like this, and it was held together with a little bit of bandage from the belly; and I had not remembered this chapter before because when masters find an unusual thing, they do not know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marsh back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the presser, with which we open the books; and to the second returns to the second questions of the two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and should be made of brass or wood; and the mouth of the funnel should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees should be one palm and a half long; and between the two joints should be two wedges of this same size, which are firmly pressed in on both sides, half a palm or more long; and these two wedges are inserted into the mouth of the marsh when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, which appears more subtle and lighter, should be made of flat iron or wood, according to the appearance of pliers; and it should have two prongs, as you see, one palm long, and two wide; and when you want to open the mouth completely with the instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet together and her legs spread apart, then push the two prongs together into the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument between her teeth; then work your hand with the instrument equally, according to the amount you want to open the mouth of the patient, until the bail does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These tools are all above, and they are multiplied in their similarities; and when the one sees them matched, the more hurried the work, and the higher the price for them by their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the tool that you have not matched, for their need is not excused.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second instrument is retained in childbirth, it must be commanded to the pain that she holds her breath, and then the faith is expelled from the condition, and both hands are held to the mouth and nose; and if she sneezes through it, well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole or covering, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as rue, anise, chamomile, cassialigne, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled over the fire; then put a cloth or covering in the pot, and the other in the mouth of the marsh, and let it sweat until the vapors come into the mouth; then make him spit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second attempt fails.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and is not better, command the bath attendant to moisten her right hand with oil of sesame or mussel oil, and then put it in the natural position, and try the second attempt; and when she has found it, grasp it and extend it gently and correctly, so that the marsh does not tear at extraction; but it should be moved slightly to the right and left, and then pull; if it comes out and disappears.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the bouche of the marris is strained, we have said the cure of expectoration, and fumigation of herbs; and if she does not have all that we have said, then guard that you do not follow the advice; but it is necessary that what is at the bouche of the marris, that you tie to the neck of the woman, then clinderize with the ointment tetrafarmaçon; if she will bear and remit, and come again healthy; but nevertheless, when she will bear if it comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and bleeds the pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary to use inconvenient fumigations for this: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to smoke the woman during retention of flowers and the second part is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is similar to a needle, and one puts the head subtly into the nature, and the ones wide above the fire; and the smoking is over the charcoal, and the lice until they are destroyed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not pierced the foundation, but it has been stopped by some subtle swelling: therefore one must then apply a lance to that swelling at its proper angle, and do not pierce too deeply, and cover the wound so it does not touch it; then put on a soft cloth with wine and oil, then the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not set, put or plug a splint, and let it remain for some time, and let it be bandaged as the child wishes to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this swelling of pus from a wound or an abscess; if it covers the wound: if it is treated, as we have said of the splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodular and thicker than those that come from above the foundation, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodulation is ancient, it works, and becomes moister with white or subtle pus, and these fistulas are never cured; and they are known by the fact that there is egestion or ventosities when the pain makes egestion, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pass through the bladder, and through half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the hip, and through the anus.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the base, and not passing through: and it is that you prick your index finger or base, and insert a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, if you insert a thin tent of lead, or horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no perforation egestion, ventosity, or ver, as we have said: saiches that it does not pierce through; then hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent near the bladder or near the urethra, if it allows urine to pass, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated near the coccyx, then the tendon comes from the bone; if there is no twisting and the location of the pain is not clear, then it is that it is attached to the bone, and there is no healing by medicine or by cauterization; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of those who try.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not ancient, with hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the pains are hidden between your hands on its back; and the legs are raised up to its knees, and its knees are bent towards its belly; then bring a tent of lead, or tin if there is twisting, until you remove the tent.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain around the base, then you should insert your index finger, feeling as if you are pushing through the skin; and if you sense between your fingers the sinew or bone, then cut it off; if not, do not force it, as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is possible to heal almost anyone, but this rarely happens; and the aid that is done, it is as if you heat the subtle cauterizer according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and bring all of it out through the fistula, until it comes near the base; and do this two or three times, until you see that these charred parts are burned away, which are similar to an arrowhead; then treat the wound with ointment, until those charred parts are gone, then treat the wound with a poultice of herbs.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is otherwise healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is not otherwise healthy; and if he has an abscess between his fingers, and does not pierce it at its base, and between his finger and the abscess a thick covering of charcoal or sawdust, and you see the fistula pointing towards the covering of the cure; if the copper of the beginning of the fistula, and before the covering, and then the cauterize after, until it reaches the top of the covering; and he will be delivered from the abscess, and closed; then wash away those charred pieces that seem like a quill of an eagle, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you cannot remove it, and cut between yourself and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization assembles two things: to wit, the burning of these charred pieces, and the stopping of blood and the removal of moisture; then cure tents boiled in butter or in broken chocolate, until the wound is filled with the burned pieces, and the charred pieces are in the wound; then cure the wound of soaking bandages with hard charcoal, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from the foundation, and is far from the body, and if you push your thumb or foundation, and inquire within.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and there are two threads or sutures or charcoal near where it is about to pierce, if there is no other way than hope and faith, by the administration of one of the three methods: whether you cauterize as we have said, or you cut just above the foundation, or if you can put tents and cure as before; and do not move too much in front, so that you do not cover the tenant who holds the foundation, and bring the excretions out through the way of willingness; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and wipe it clean after it is cut above the foundation, or by tent or other appointed instrument; then clean the char that is in the wound, as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound and to delay the fistula in the part before the foundation: if there is a lighter thing to the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you push the tent into the fistula, it is where it costes on the foundation below the skin above, then take a tent perceived at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And if you push the thread into the fistula, and push the tent along the entire thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is not in the margin of the foundation within, then push the thread of that which is perforated, so that you push your other or foundation; and take the head of the thread, and bring together the two parts together, and hold one against the other, and leave it for a day or two; and do not restrain it once, until the thread covers those which are between the two, and heal; then cure the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then I will perforate it in all possible ways that you can, unless it is too deeply seated.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not matter to make the adjustment overly deep if it is deeply seated, and then treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny backbone from which the fistula is made should be much and of one piece, part and branching; on the other hand, not, because we do not know what we should not know, as you see here:
des emorroydes	desmorroids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they have blood, and there are one or more, and they are deficient in the foundation and at the base of the foundation; but those that are deficient have little moisture, and are covered with a little sharp orange or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh; and the treatment of those inside the foundation is that you command the patient to sweat so he can go to other rooms, as long as the foundation is full, and they open; if you hurry, and you can hold them with pliers, or you hold them with your finger, then you cut at their roots; and if they cannot be held by their moisture, take them to the cloth, or to the cotton, or a piece of cloth; and hold them in your two hands, then cut, and powder over some hot powders that are in the cauterant; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterants, so they are treated with other treatments until they are healed; and if the foundation cannot come out, clean the patient with a rough cloth to wash what is inside the foundation, so it can come out openly; and if the hemorrhoids swell, and the filaments are full of the foundation, then the treatment is light; and it is that you hold them with your finger or with pliers, and cut, then treat as we have said, until they are healed, and do not fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to stitch the wound according to this method: take a thread of twisted hair, and bend it into an needle, and then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread away from the needle, and if it is too wide; and straighten the thread formally, then loosen the thread, and remove the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one to let the excess blood out; then put above the wound a cloth moistened in rose oil or in cerate, and put above the wound, and command the patient to rest; and then let him rest until they are healed, and when they are healed, treat them with ointment and other treatment, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryly and without moisture at the foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often occur in the intestines due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to reset at the point of a spatula or at your angle, which does not allow moisture; then treat it as it should be while it is dry; and if it cannot be treated, then begin the scraping more forcefully than before until it is healed, and then scrape; then treat it as it should be while it is clean.
dou fremit	dry heat
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mice are a small appearance found at the back, and it moves quickly; and sometimes it finds the bone, and one feels like fever, and it spreads throughout the body, and more so in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a needle of a goose quill, or a needle of a vulture very strong, and place that needle on the fever, until the circle pressing the fever all around; then turn your hand to all the needle so that you cover all around the fever, and pull it forward, and extract the fever from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, then make a thorn of a needle of rain or iron in this form, and be subtle to remove and bring up:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Never pierce, to hold the two together, and press it. And if you see, if cauterize the wound, as it is before or in the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of this ointment
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never made an ointment of silver or copper, or lead melted or crushed; and never made of these small and large instruments, according to those which they are accustomed to use.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those which they should use in the care of children and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large ointment is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a dislocation where the belly is twisted, as you see, and the ribs are broken on one side and one on the other; and the belly is filled with medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and there are small holes all around, and between each hole there should be one inch of space, then pull on these holes with a strong thread, and tie the belly together as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the ribs are broken by an instrument before a strong thread, then suture them like a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with a cloth of oil or a similar thing, then gently apply it; then the assistant applies it to both hands together, until it is all visible, then remove the cloth, and relieve the pain in his legs, and if the swelling wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply the cloth in the illness of diarrhea of the belly, and the medicine wants to come out, then restart it as long as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the thorn is in the foundation or abscess, it should be removed as delicately as for a child; and this is the form of the delicate removal above with the skin being stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatment of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different depending on how they are made, and depending on the limbs or wounds that are made, and for what reason they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by being pierced with a spear, and cut with a sword or dagger, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the limbs of the body, such as a wound that occurs above the neck, or on the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you about the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	When a simple wound comes or the bone is not broken, be careful if it is a piercing or similar things, and if the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of an abscess: if you do it immediately cleanse the head itself if there is little blood from the wound, and cleanse the opposite side if the wound is large; and avoid the pains of repletion of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to cleanse, let him eat light food, and do not drink wine, and do not change his diet; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in sterilizing wine; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder that I will say a little later; and if the wound has been moved, put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a spear wound and similar, and the lips cannot be sewn together by tenting, then sew them together by stitching, as I will say about belly wounds, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, and can be moved, but only held by a little, then cover it with a copper; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat soft foods, such as meat and bread, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you remove or cut off the skin entirely, and there is no bone, then cover the whole with copper, and pour in foul matter, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting it, and it cannot be stanched by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you remove the arrow, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should put in this powder that boils as soon as the wound comes into contact with it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; fresh chalk three parts, and the powder finely ground, and fill the wound, and bind it tightly, until it has healed well and joined to all its skin; then bandage it well, and leave it untouched, unless it swells; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one should never use chalk alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound has not been moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound has moved, immediately apply this powder; but if it has not moved, place some ointments digested with onions or poultices of flour of barley made with honey and water, until it is healed; then treat with other cures until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then strain it with fine needles; and I will tell you about the main fractures afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes from the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and the main fracture, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a bone, there is no other method than to let the care, and not put anything restricting, because it hurts bones and makes them retract; and do not put anything sharp on the wound, for the substance of bones is cold, and its continuation with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be gentle, as wine washed in hot sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and the cloth washed in hot sweet water, and other stones of this manner, and gently moist.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bandage it and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and the bone is exposed and filled with pus, then drill or go deeper into the bone; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then drain it, and clean it, and cauterize it as necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the wound is deep, and the vein is exposed, keep it away from the meat as it goes down the side of the neck, and do not touch the neck but put it back according to its natural shape; then slowly tighten it, and leave it for some time, then cure dressings as long as they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, try to remove them all, and those that you cannot remove, leave until the wound can heal and be aligned; and if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if he has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of arrow or of dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound of arrow or of dagger, and the wound is deep, look to see if from the wound there is ventosity that the hairs are all out: cut then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh at all its blood, do not put in the first hour the powder, or the bandage for the blood that it does not stick to the flesh, and return to the heart, and occlude the pain; but put attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put in the wound old cotton to draw out the moisture, and make the pain sleep on the wound three times a day, or four, or more; then there will not be any spasm, nor trembling of the heart from anything else; and when you see the good dispositions, cut that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds and other treatments until they are healed; and if they cannot be healed and worked on, then create a fistula; as the cure should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from an incision of a sword or knife, and it is simple, or pierced through the front or back, then treat as the cure for what is in front; if it is large, stitching; and if it is small, powder, and if it has been pushed into the bone, and has broken off pieces, then apply to the wound, and remove any foreign bodies if they are necessary; and if they are not necessary, let the wound rot, so that it will align with the extraction; and for other wounds in other limbs is according to judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	belly rupture
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is large and medium and small; from the great wound, once the intestines or the nerves of the intestines escape, by which the puncture of them; and the sewing is more harmful, and once the small wound is worse than the big one, because one should not put the intestines back in, unless they are put back in exactly as they were; for the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, if they are put back in more carefully, and for this reason, the medium-sized wound is worse, because one must suture the intestines to their place as with other II And there are four ways that the rupture of the belly is according to: the two common seams are in the seam of the belly, and the seam of other wounds of the body and II other special seams are common to other wounds; and nevertheless, they are more special with the seam of the belly, and I will say one by one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is injured, and it is easy to set, it is done by one of the two methods: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen by the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, heat the intestines in this manner: moisten a sponge or some wool soaked only in cold water, or cook in boiling hot and copper and spike, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and never do this with force, and it is better to let it cool slowly.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, if the intestine is moist or dry and badly cooked, because by this the entrance is soon; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision with the instrument with which one copes with worms; and the first care is to still the pain, that we should not cut without great necessity where there is none; and this is the tool for cutting: if you cut inside the belly and outside, and draw out the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, if you can put it back according to its natural form in its own place, because this is helpful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part outside the abdomen, it is necessary that you place the injured side on top of the patient's back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part outside the abdomen, raise the head and the worst part higher than the other parts, and thus manage as I said for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wounds are small, place what is appropriate on top of them, then apply ointments that cover the entire wound with their hands, and bring together the lips; this is the common method for stitching, and it is that you press a needle or several, depending on the size of the wound, leaving about an inch from the edge of the wound, and then insert a needle with strong thread; then pierce the two layers of skin with the two layers of flesh, which is outside the skin, until you make it perforated from that part, and bring together the two layers of flesh the four times; then bind the wound with a double thread around the needle on both sides, then evenly sew up the wound, leaving about an inch, and then insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you have done with the needles until the entire wound is closed; and let the needles be of medium size, between thin and thick, because thin needles cover the entire wound, and thick ones cannot enter well: for this reason they should be medium; and do not insert the needles too far on the other side of the skin and flesh, so that they do not cut and open the wound before sewing; then cover the edges of the wound with the needle, so that they do not bleed at night, and put bandages or cloths on the edges of the needle to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is sewn; this method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires one or two needles for the second stitch, which is common, and it is that you bring together the two layers of skin and the two layers of flesh to a needle with a strong thread; and when you have pierced these edges all four times, then insert the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner of sewing needles; and leave about an inch between each stitch.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestines because it had been 24 hours since they were removed, and the wound was dressed after 15 days, and treated, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the miracle worker thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I applied silk cotton wool twice a day over the wound, and washed it with honey until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two main ways of stitching: take the needle, and the thread from the part in front of the skin; when it has pierced through the curved part correctly, then put the head of the suture or the stitch where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the other side of the part inside the skin; and the understanding of this stitching is that you stitch as the furriers do the pelts, and that you leave one end of the suture on one part, and bring it out on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galen properly calls, is such that anyone can do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the main needles to the other main needle, in a similar manner: stick a needle or main needle close to the wounded part, and make it pierce only that part alone, and leave the two wounds of the syfac; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the front part just above, the two wounds of the syfac; then make it pierce both from the front part just above, in two other needles that are on the other side; and this is the easiest way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens say this word, and no one testifies to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, or one in each; and one should put one needle on one side and the other on the other, in the manner of those who embroider corroies; and sutures that when the tear is in the belly, it is sewn more painfully than other stitches of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you probe the fresh wound to its blood, as soon as the doctor has moved it, you put back the intestine and the gut; then put powder in the char, and if the doctor has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound closes; and stitch the wound, and be careful of the sifac and the mirach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on cotton wool, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For in other medical conditions with many different wounds, when the wound is simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not have communication with the principal members, then it is necessary to apply a light oil of moderate heat, or rose oil, and put it around the angles, and rub it on the joints; and if it causes pain or inflammation in the belly, and often happens, then you should dress it with black wine, and immediately if the inflammation comes to the intestines; and pierce it inside, and scrape out what is inside, as when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is bare, and this is because of the smallness of the veins that are in it, and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and its approach to the nature of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the tendon jumps from the wound, it should be replaced as the intestine when it is fresh; and if it is old and turned black, then you must tie the limb that has turned black, because there are veins and arteries in it; then cover what is between the ligament, and hang the two threads from the part outside the wound to the other side to equalize the extraction when the tendon breaks, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breaking of a boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is punctured, and the wound is small, if it can be restored to some people, because I saw that one man was gutted from his stomach by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became an abscess, and in it there was excretion and ventosity; I put care according to what I could, and did not cease to subtilize until it was healed, and the people recovered.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healing, I doubted that the hairs were not in his intestine; and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, and fed and watered; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such a way: take a sharp needle, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the needle has opened the mouth, put it above the two lips, so that it holds its mouth above; then cover the wound, and hold it so that it cannot slip, then put the other sharp needle in that way before, until the wound is completely closed; and through the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the shoulder blade burns inside, and no harm comes to the hairs, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this intestine thread that is very dirty, and then tie it to the end of this thin thread of linen, then wind the thread around the needle, and pull the intestine through, and sew it in the tear; and this method of stitching is no more than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no skill or remedy, only subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	that all wound or abscess, when it is covered, is universally called "fistula", and specifically when it is cut and opened up.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the veracity of the nodation removed hard and white, where no pain is felt, and it is cut open like a quill of an eagle; and sometimes it is clear and open, and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes enough; and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that all wound that is not healed, and there is no pus, except by one of the VIII causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or by its malice; or because there is hard pus inside, and on the lips, that does not let new pus grow; or there is too much pus; or the wounds are poisoned, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late healing, and flows by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to inform you of the treatment of fistulas that is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to large veins, and to arteries, and to nerves, or to the face, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the main member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this kind are a difficult healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the bone that I have said, and you have firm knowledge of the cure, and you know how to treat it, if the fistula is straight, take a lead or iron tent, if it is crooked, take a subtle cloth tent, for the plasters adhere well to the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot heal it well with tents, then suture one of the holes, for the moisture does not pass from one hole to another, and cleanse it; then treat it properly, knowing whether there is bone or nerve, and it is close to the joint, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it; and when you will know truly where it is, and whether it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, treat it according to what I have told you, and remove the corrupt matter and the charred parts that are inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply located at the right place, then cut it open as much as you can, then put moist tents in medicine, and fill them with water as close to the fistula as possible, until the medicine corrodes the remaining matter; and then apply ointments of clean, sound char, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves cause you pain or injury to your main limbs, as we have said; and if the tooth is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove the corruption until it is completely removed, then cure the things in the same way as before until they are healed; and if they are not healed, and remain as before, cut off that part which you were sent to do: if it reveals and wants to be removed for as long as you can bear, and remove all the corruption, then restore the tooth; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, then it is too deep, and you cannot reach it; there is no other means than to wait for nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with forceps, and if there are many bones, then take them all, and do not leave any behind; and if the moisture makes it against you, and there is no error or fear, then cope and moisture and heat, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something in the wound that promotes putrefaction, and let it stay around the bones until they are softened; and then they will be more easily broken. And if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, raise the corruption as far as the bone is not entirely ossified, then reopen the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption, and comes just below the bone; if it is necessary, cover all around the corruption, and then cure it until it is sound. And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of around 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, so that the matters came to the leg and he was filled with a large abscess, and there was no apparent reason to open it; but the maker by their folly opened it so high that the abscess opened, and they drew out much matter, and became a fistula, and there was much pus coming from the body; and many more sought cure within two years, and there was no healing in the art of hands, until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was coming out through the fistula was great pus; and the young man's body became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and found that one was coming towards the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore withdrew, and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming to the bone from within; I saw that the rotten bone appeared to me, and I thought there was no other corruption except what I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with salves for a long time, but I could not heal it; then I returned, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and I saw it, and then I removed it, and I was unable to heal the limb; but I could only cut around a palm of the bone, and treat it all over its length, then I treated it with salves; and it became sound and healed quickly, and it did not require further treatment except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because for the evacuation of blood, it often occurred, but he was completely healed, and in the place of the bone, a hard char was born, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contrary at all, neither to the other nor to the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take a ligature, and stretch it at the head of the bone that opens, and command that it be extended up; and put another thicker band than the first band on top of the first band, and tie it above the char that is on the bone, and extend the head, so that you remove the corrupted char from the outside, and uncover the char above the place where you want to be, so that it does not corrupt the char; and put a tissue or a pad outside the bone to cover the corrupted char; and it should be done so that one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again.
