Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the tooth is decayed and does not open, and the decay is in the middle or in one part, remove the entire tooth; then apply the tison on both sides of the corruption, and sew from one part to the other the corruption, and keep the suture long enough near the corruption as we have said; and if the decay is in the joint, cut away the corrupted part of the joint, and sew the bone or what contains it from the other side; and if the decay is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other means but to cover them; and if the decay is on the fingertip or on the tip of the toe, this is a very difficult thing, but nevertheless you should inquire how the corrosion opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve do anything against it; and know that the tools for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of their teeth, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore you should prepare a tool for each kind of work, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so think about the tool that you have in hand according to what it should be.
dou feu	heat
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The members will rot either due to lack of blood or due to lack of air; and when you have treated the corrosion with medicine, and it does not improve, then you must amputate the member up to the joint where the corrosion comes from, so that the pain escapes through the wound, or through the malice, which is greater, due to the lack of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, so that it seems as if they were burned by fire, and afterwards becomes darker, then those corrosions spread from member to member, and take hold throughout the body; if you delay in covering it, and if the corrosion is at the head of the toe, then cover it, and do not give it any space for the poison to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes from the hand, if the cloth is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the cloth is at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy other than the quantity of its virtue; and thus do as follows when the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes in the first joint, if the cloth after the other joint; and if it comes or pierces, if the cloth all the piercing; and if it goes up the leg, if the cloth at the hip joint; and if it comes above the hip, there is no other remedy than to let the hurt member lie down and out, and extend some ministers one of the limbs below, and some other ministers the other limb above, and uncover the cartilage between the two limbs to a span wide, until the bone is exposed; then the cloth or bandage, and put on each part of the linen, so that the hurt member does not touch the clean skin, and comes to the other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood comes out when you are working, cauterize the limb firmly, or put some powders that stop the bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his eye: he had a black eye that looked like fire burning, and that corrosion first came into his eye, and it took over the whole eye; and when the other saw the corrosion, he covered his eye, and was healed; and later on, the corrosion came from the other side of the hand, and it came to me, and I put some things that reflect after cleaning the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he thought I would cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope to reflect the matter; and he also doubted if I cut off his hand, that he would not die, because the power of the man was weak; and he desperately gave up, and returned to his land, and covered his hand, and was healed; and I did not tell anyone else except for what is done in such cases.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes an abscess in a thin limb, and it lasts so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; then it bursts and pierces, and the pus escapes, as if it were a bag; and the skin above is also as delicate as cloth, and does not corrode the bone, nor the nerve, and such diseases are called "sinuses", and are not called "fistulas"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from the outside, it is called a "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cut all around it, and immediately when it is delicate, as if it were cloth; and it does not corrode for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the skin is burned and the corruption is not yet fully formed, and the skin is charred, then use this ointment: look to see if the breasts are large, and the nipple is foul-smelling, then use the Egyptian ointment made as follows: take aloe, oil, and frankincense equally, and mix them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then take according to your need, and make it into an eagle and honey, and use it to cleanse the breasts, and hold the nipple; leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by splashing; do this many times until the breasts are cleansed and the pus is drained; if the pain cannot be borne, and the Egyptian ointment and the ash of cinders do not help, then use an ointment of honey and water with a little litargire broken up; or use an ointment of honey and melted wine, where the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the skin soft; when you have done this, and you are sure the breasts are cleansed, then use an ointment of rose oil and wine; if the nipple is small, and the ointment cannot enter, then enlarge it with a needle a little, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is large enough; if the wound is too large, then leave it alone until the skin or the ointment can enter, and if the nipple that is above is foul-smelling, then cover it with a cloth or lower down where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the wound is in the front, do not allow any char to enter; and if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, then apply medicines that will help the wound heal, and place them on a linen cloth that covers the entire wound; then cover the wounded area with a larger cloth on the other side of the first one, according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound to align it, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days; and whoever is on the other side of the wound, often remove it to align the wound, and observe what comes out of the wound, whether it is poison or little or enough, or digested or undigested; and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in this way for a while and you see that nature is taking over, then remove the cloth and approach the wound; and then remove the bandage in the morning or the next day, and when you remove the bandage, change the other cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts are not digested well after many hours, cut them so that the breasts do not swell.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are cut after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people who take long to heal from wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if the breasts are not digested well after many hours, cut them so that the breasts do not swell; and if the breasts are slow to heal and are distant, use moist substances and dry virtues, such as oil of rose, and vinegar equal in substance; then cook and use it; and this same thing is also good for growing wounds, when there is no oil of roses present, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and the powder on the honey when it is over the fire; and then apply it to the wound, and never administer an aristocrat long and blue lily roots, which is also like flour and a hundred; and use simple or compound: grind them and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is long and not cured by this cure, then cut out the corruption, and press into the bone, or hard members, or limbs; if the cure of the wound is like what we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the pocket of the hand, or foot, or perhaps in other places; and when it is released, and no care is taken, if the abscess comes out, and corrodes and weeps blood so much that it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps corrodes it entirely; and then there are corrosions up to the bone, as long as there is painful putrefaction, and the affected part is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, then you must remove all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauteries are very great help if the bones are healthy and the joint is sound; but if the joint is close to the flesh, and begins to prick and bleed, it is necessary that you put a piece of cloth outside the joint that does not touch the flesh, and bring the blood upwards, and gently and carefully cover this wound with hot and corrosive medicines until all is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cover it and drain, for as much as the bone decays and is, it cannot be healed; and if you see the other decaying, cover it with a cloth as previously mentioned, then cure until it is healed; and if it is fierce, and bleeding, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you first stop the bleeding; then cover the joint with a thin layer of herbs in cutting across, and make sure the cut does not reach the flesh outside the joint, for the hairs would feel too much pain; and if there is, put something on top to ease.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand must be sharp
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The shoulders that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all charred, and by chance they have a tail or where they have bones, and once they have an angle, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in any of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born in none of the two joints do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the shoulder may move; the tail of the charred one is light, like this: cut it off at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you hold it with a copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the back out, it is necessary that you first cut the round bone around the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk for this, then care for it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same things that come together in two ways come from birth or from the wound healing process, or from burning of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut the one that is healing, so that it returns to its natural forms; then put between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so that it does not heal; or you put between two pieces of thin leather, until the wounds are healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it comes to either of his two hands with the palm, then apply the cure as it should be done.
des vils	of the fingers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large and swollen, filled with excess melancholy, which often come in many members of the body; and more so in legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should never administer any purgation of clay, and then give the healthy one from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is done in two ways: one is to apply it, and draw out the black blood; and the other way is to open the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The belly is done in this way: first, the first leg of high hot water very strongly, until the big without being subtly removed, then straighten the leg with the bad from above the hip to the part below the groin; then cut the vein in I or II or III, a wide incision, then release and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one to the other, until so much blood can be suffered by the virtue of the bad; and then tie it, and command him to stain himself with meat boiled in black broth; and then repeat the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are flat and no longer bleed.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. The fire cauterization should instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the eye is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must torment it to unravel it, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have previously described.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one covers the eye if it is curved, and does not cut through, so that it does not cover the vein; and it is of large size, because if it were fine, it would cover the vein, but if it is large as we have said, this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the vein civilian
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is opened in the legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in land that has no moisture; and by chance it is opened in other parts than the legs, and this happens from the pus that comes out of the skin, as it comes from within the flesh and muscles, open between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the limb changes, and the wound begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound opens, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of cloth of one and a half inches wide and long enough to cover the wound, and the wound, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not there, if it is wrapped around the cloth, and the wound; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the remaining, and do not cover it at its root, until it is all out; for if you cover it, it will go back into the wound, and cause abscess and putrefaction or swelling, and serious disease; therefore it is necessary that it be treated little by little from the top, and nothing remains or remains inside; and this wound never occurs when it is treated with length of hand or ten, and some have come to me, because it issued from ten inches long, and when you cover it, if the pain or pus, and perforate through the bottom, so that everything is out; and let the matter inside be drained, and administer medicines for putrefaction every day, then the cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein, and even when it opens into the joint of the little finger, or the big toe, and much blood comes out, and it jumps back; therefore, as we have said before, treat it accordingly.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of verses that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cow disease," because it often occurs in cows, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and is felt all over the body from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it went, and jumps out; and it is caused by the corruption of some humors, such as worms and roundworms and tapeworms and intestinal worms; and its evil is doubtful, because as it goes through the body, and goes up to the head, and comes to the oil, perhaps it enters, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the patient and treat them, it is not possible to do otherwise than when they go: therefore it is necessary to hold the limb above and away from a very tightly bound limb, then cut into it and remove it, and if it comes out in front of the char, and you do not remove it, then cauterize with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrodes the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, then hold it away from it firmly, then cut into it and remove it; and it is necessary to use the remedy of healing of the bodies of soluble medicines for the bad humors that are thrown out, and if there is a war against foods in order to cure putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "windiness", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from member to member; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered that one of her arms was swollen; and soon after, I saw a small blister in the vein of the arm; and then, as soon as anything, like quick silver when it cuts through leather, the pain departed from that arm, and went into the shoulder, and then, a little while later, it spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she had turned around inside her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how the disease moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this illness in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had heard that it could move from one limb to another, but I had not seen it in this way before; and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, and because that apparent constraint appeared; and it did not appear in this way to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease and the pain feels as we have said, if it appears to you as we have described, then pull the limb back and forth quickly, and then cover it with a cloth until that constraint is released from the limb; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes, then treat the cause of the veins as we have said, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their likenesses and according to the places where they enter.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hooked ones, and smeared ones; and those with two angles, and those with tails, and those with pieces; and the one that enters any member as follows: if it enters a principal member, such as the neck, head, heart, lung, kidneys, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it enters any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about afterwards, appears: then it is necessary that you attempt the extraction of this arrow, for death comes in many ways; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not completely removed, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	When the arrowhead enters the skull and pierces the bone, and the spasm that is above the brain occurs, which is blindness and dizziness and sweating and trembling of the limbs, and inflammation and trembling of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and possibly without strength in the nose or ears; and possibly with loss of speech and voice; and a white discharge from the wound like pus, and also like dripping blood; and if this sign appears to you, then hold the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The symptoms of a broken bone when it breaks or cracks are that it is near the right breast, and also feels like it is stuck in something hard, without any movement; and by chance the bone moves like a chicken, and there is black blood, and cold sweat, and syncope: therefore, without doubt, the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow has not been removed is that without any complaint of pus, it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the limb changes color, and it breathes high and seeks the heat.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead enters the covering of the worst place, it is below the small ribs; and it pours out much blood and great pain and breathlessness; and they move all the member of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead enters the stomach, by chance if it jumps from the wound nothing of the undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead enters the belly, and it does not pierce any part of the intestines, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead enters the bladder, and the urine pours out and comes out afterwards, and the pain is very great: it is certain that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and back and spine and hip and knee and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that hit him in the root of the knee: I tried to remove it, and pulled it out from the other side through the ear fat, and he was cured without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And to a patient who had an arrow in the fat of the oil paper outside, and the arrow was placed, and it could not reach further than the tip towards the fust, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all iron without ears; the wound was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And to a Christian who had an arrow in his throat, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I cut off the barbs, and carefully removed it until I took it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And to a man who had an arrow in his head or stomach, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days without changing his condition; I cut into the wound, and pressed it, and removed it, and no bad accident came to him.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to help a person who has an arrow stuck in them or their back, and the wound was sown up over; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, nor found harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to help another person who had an arrow stuck in their face, and the wound was sown up over; and it remained thus to suffer great pain; and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And if you have an arrow stuck in the face of the king, which is bent downwards towards the left side; and it is leaning slightly to the right part; and the arrow is completely set straight, I was called to cure after it had been bent for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I applied a thin gauze to it, and I felt nothing; but he felt pricking and pain outside his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow; I applied a blistering ointment to his forehead, because the swellings did not subside; and the swellings of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the ointment again later, and it immediately relieved the pain, and the swellings lasted a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed the medicine of ague corrosive on the wound with my hands, as long as it was open, and I probed it, and felt the point of the arrow which was lodged in the flesh; then I poured in the medicine of ague through the opening of the wound, until the point of the arrow appeared visibly; and it passed well through the four months, and then it discharged itself when I pulled out the arrows, and one from one side and the other, and could not be removed; therefore I did not cease to subtilize and engineer in various ways of instruments, until I got a good set of arrows, according to what its form would come at the end of this chapter, so that I could extract it and heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the miracle worker judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it then, and it was sewn up, and the pain was healed completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you might place your care above what I do not say, for the books cannot comprehend everything; but the wise masters present and absent know many things, and know what is present and lacking, to find new work, and new tool, in the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from members or are discharged in two ways: either by the way they enter, or by another part; and the one that comes out by the way it enters, is an arrow entering into its own flesh, and has never been removed.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her remain until the charcoal is thoroughly rotted and the issue is ready; and likewise if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot escape, let her remain thus for some time, and move her every day; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, pierce all around until the forest is subtly penetrated, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the belly's ventricles, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: if you do not draw it out, but let her remain thus for some time after, because if the arrow comes towards the brain, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not embedded in the bone only, and does not come out immediately, and remains in place for several days without causing harm, then pull it out with an engine.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be pulled out, then administer tar to surround it as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the flesh and cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the tent; and if you feel it, then remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot pull it out due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, sinew, or vein, then leave it until the wound becomes large; and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has ears attached to it that hold it in place, then cut the thread that is deeply embedded on both sides of the wound, and then break or crush the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out; but be careful not to break the arrow while removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, then pull the limb back to its place, for the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding from the vein makes it difficult, follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and avoid the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put effort as you are able to draw the arrow without risk, or quickly or slowly, or firmly or violently; and put the hairs according to the form it was when the arrow fell out, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place so that one can see or feel it: cut then above, as much as the hooks can take, and then extract it: if it suddenly fired now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, round your hand and push it into the bone, until it enters the bone, and expand the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if it is of the arrow and is, if it has been pushed in, and you administer slowly, if it is administered with a tool, so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the tool; and then push further, and if the arrow is caught, if it is pushed in, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as it should be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is stuck in the chest or abdomen or bladder or side, and it is close, and you can cut through it, then cut above it, but do not cut the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then treat the wound if necessary; and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the needles used to extract arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and this is their shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrow's tip is like the beak of a bird, to place at the point of the arrow, as follows:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the nails to hold and to fix is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins that one can bleed from, of which there are 16 main ones, namely: two veins behind the ears, called the "ear veins"; and the two arteries in the temples; and the two veins in the arm pits, called the "aspirated" veins; and the vein in the forehead; and the vein at the root of the nose; and the two jugular veins; and the two veins in the neck; and the two veins in the lips, which are called the "agelic" veins; and the two veins outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are usually opened are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the right side, and it is called "the main vein of the head" by some people; and the middle one is called "the forearm vein", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and it is called "the vein of the body" by some people; and the basilic is on the left side, and it is called "the stomach vein", and it is above the fossa, and it is the one that is usually opened, which opens manifestly over the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the auricular and the annular, and it is in the right arm; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is outside the corbeure of the pouch on the right side, and the second one is at the ankle of the left costeit; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other costei; and in the other leg there are three veins.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	For the veins behind the ears, it helps with ancient enemas and headaches; and the qualities of this treatment, as I have said, and it is that you remove the main pain, and rub the ear or the vein with a rough cloth; then squeeze the veins with a string to a pin, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two holes of the ear: then apply it to your other ear, and where you feel the hair of your other ear, if it is blocked; then take the lancet, and push it out from the ear to the bone, then lift your hand up on the ear, and rub and the skin and the ear well twice through, and make the blood flow until you see; then stop and tie, as long as it is healed; and I have already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The vein puncture in the two temples is best done by an experienced, skilled, and accustomed person, and who knows how to hold the eyes steady so they do not move; and the quality of the puncturer is as I said: that the hairs are strangely stretched out, pulling the veins apart; and it feels like the hair is detached from the skin, then sign of the needle, then lift the skin over the vein at the top of the index finger, and remove the needle from outside, and lift the skin over the vein, and cover it, as you have done in the other veins, and draw out the blood according to your necessity; then release the pain, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then bandage it, and let it be healed; and we have spoken of its puncturing, its covering, and its extraction, which begins this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sainie of the frontal vein is as valuable as the sainie of the cephalic diseases, ancient facial diseases, and migraines; and the quality is such that the pains are strange, twisting their neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called «fosseur», which has the following form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point above the vein, and hold it firmly with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you see; then release the neck from the pain, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again in one wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	For the flames should not be too hot or sharp, and the iron should be flat, because the bone is close, and by chance it may break the flames when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The second vein that is in the two arms helps with the elbows, and the wrist, and the hand, and the palm, and the face; and the quality of their iron is such that the pain is strange when twisting from any limb, as before; then the iron, and let the iron be flat, a little long with the flame, a little wide, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the flame is too fine, perhaps it might break; then correct the blood, as much as you have skill, and then tie it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein's blood is good against fever, and against swelling, and against diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that comes in the face, and always when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that the pains strain their neck, then strain their neck to your right hand, and take the fine flame long, and make it into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in the nose, and the sinuses begin to heal now; and do not move too much in front, and correct the blood according to your need, then tie it for one night, because it is soon restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The oil of the two junipers helps to narrow the nostrils, and at the beginning of sneezing, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosion, and in herpes, and in lichen; and the quality of the oil is such that the hairs strain their necks on one side and the other, as we have said; and so the masters are above the chief of the hairs, and the hairs sit on one seat, then clean the long one with a little width, then draw the blood temperately, or as much as the matter requires; then do the other part in the other nostril, then remove the lint, and strain the nostrils evenly, that the hairs do not strangle; and leave it just before morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips above helps to cool in the mouth, and prevents corruption of the gums, and cracks of the lips, and soreness and swelling around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of this health is to make the pain sit in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at both the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: therefore match both of them, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt, match the largest of each part, and do the same with both the veins that are above and below, for it is one way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are outside the tongue helps after the health of the head, and it is in the tightness of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healer is that the diseases cease between your hands before the sun, and you lift the tongue, and look at each side a black vein: healthy therefore both, and do not go too far, for outside are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins that are commonly healed are healed in two ways: either by pinching at all the flame mertin wide, or by slicing thinly as they cut through, and is called "anesil"; and they are wide and thin according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has the task of opening closed veins plainly deep with thick blood and turbulent; and this is the form of the flame mirror.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more delicately pointed, and is for cleaning thin veins, where there is thin blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The cleansing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and shoulder, and arm, and abdomen; and it is necessary for the cleaner to clean properly, and to remove the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the tendon, and blood flows, then it should be cooled, as I have said; and it should not be pricked with fire, but cut as with a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the priest does not clearly open it, then you should force it and change to another; or you want any blood from it, or you save in its place the vein of the arm: it opens clearly; and he copes with the fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the joint of the vein, then it is also necessary to force the arm until you feel the pulse; then sign the joint of the elbow, and then bind the arm, and cope the vein with the fire as we have said; and be careful not to strike in the artery when you see the joint swells, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding upwards as high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, then it is from an artery: hurry then, and place your finger on it long, then remove your finger slowly, as many times as it has bled; hold the arm still, and let it not move the bad parts; and be patient, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and you feel pain, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery open, for the main part of it will retreat; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a sharp knife, and cut it, and take one of the halves and lay it firmly against the other; if it is not wet, that is good; if not, then the healer, as we have said, applies powders that stop bleeding; and the bandages do not become gray in many positions for the small wound of the sore, and the position of the little arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle helps to treat blood from the main vein and the body, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the saint to search for the vein that is out, and if it does not appear too quickly, and he finds the vein, and he inflates it and the wound becomes gray, and perhaps it cannot be healed; and this vein opens often, and if it does not open in any men because of its subtlety, then you must use the saint's instrument to open it; and shield the vein from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The puncture of the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head and helps with the eyes; and it is best to puncture at the olive oil or mustard flame, for this is the safest of all veins, as it has no nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is best to ask for the lightest vein, and do not cause any harm if it does not work the first time, and start again; and perhaps the veins swell in some people, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you need to know about healing is that healing is only done to maintain health and to ward off diseases that may come; and it should be done in one of the three vessels that are in the body: namely, the cephalic, the thoracic, and the abdominal; and if you need to heal at the beginning of the day, do so in the morning, in autumn, and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion is apparent; and if you need to heal on the first or third day, do so after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sane which is administered to diseases has no determined hour, but rather when necessary is in the morning or at night, in all hours and all times; and it does not matter to sanctify children up to fourteen years, nor a woman carrying except for four months until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And they should not be sanctified much the elderly who have passed sixty years.
