Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wants to sanctify, in whatever way it is, it is necessary that he cleanses the intestines of a light clyster, if he has much retained feces, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous noxious substances to the principal members; and one should not sanctify much those who are too weak from meats, or who are pregnant, as much as they can be, nor hydropiques; and if one wants to sanctify after colic passion, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and frequent staying up late at night, and all the virtue, or by some arm or body; then subtly the humors, if it is not too thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if one has them; then enter or bath, if nothing prevents, to sanctify more the sane, and sanctify from the vein in the third hour, as we have said; and guard that day of work, and pain, and luxury, and similar things; and be tied and joined, and let the sane be higher than those who are sanctified, and let the rub the arm twice or three times, then gently move the joint above the middle, because when it is too stiff or weak, it cannot correct the vein; and then rub the hand on the forehead until the veins swell, and feel on; then moisten the sane with a little flame of old oil, then put his right hand on top of the vein of the hand uncovered wherever he wants to sanctify, that the vein does not fail to hit.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as if they were strings at the surgeon's touch, and there are some that are plain of their thinness, such that when one puts them over the flame, they retract from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are those; and if the surgeon opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, because it is necessary that the surgeon be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, then start again a little above that place or below, as long as the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the joint is swollen, and the pain subsides, leave it open for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: perhaps an abscess will form; do not enter the bath, then begin the healing if it suits him; and if the wound is small, or the skin is thin and you doubt that there is as much blood as you saw, then apply heat directly to the wound; and the work should be done gently, as long as the joint is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the joint swelling, do not begin healing again, and put a little oil on it, for it reduces the flow of blood, and is soothing in this wound like the oil; and thus administer the oil in every healing that you apply to the wounds, to stop the flow of blood; and the same applies to triacle and bowels, when put on the wound; and separate the skin gently as it becomes too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If there are large abscesses that often occur, even when they are not drained except at this time or when the opening of the vein is small, you must hurry and place a soft, moist sponge on the wound and tie it with a cloth for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the issue of the blood from the vein, and if it remains on the limb for any time without turning black or green, you must not remove it; and if you see, place anything of aloes or of myrrh mixed with honey or wine on it, as a remedy.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance of the wound at the base of the church: put your hand on it, and if you press the wound too much with your hand, that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not put anything on it that we have said, for by chance you may cut the artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the wound, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out each wound according to the amount of its virtue and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it turns red; and if you see it large, let it bleed until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is appropriate for one who is weak and unable, and has the task of extracting arrows, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and frequently heal it quickly, and it should be healed by cutting across, not by pinching; and this method of healing is safe from the separation of the arrow and the tearing of the nerve, and it is better than the healing of the long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body is prone to the wound, it is appropriate to give bread soaked in juice of pomegranates; if they are hot-blooded, take out the arrow three times or four times and then apply the bread soaked in honey syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and strong-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he pounds at the wound after much bleeding, it is necessary that he drink a broth of meat, and an aromatic syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the chapter or section on syncope for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bandage an arm, and wound it again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bind it little by little, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to bandage an arm after the first wounding, and he has great pain, he should bind it seven hours after the first wounding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wishes to heal from the other side, one must heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has much blood within the body which is already heated, and causes fever; therefore one must draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it bleeds freely; then one must address all the conditions of healing, and place one's hand on the pulse when it begins to slow, so that the patient does not die in the absence of blood, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it is never necessary to remove the arm, and draw out blood the second time, and the vein is closed, that one presses strongly against; or if it is swollen, one extends the arm gently, for this would be harmful; but one leaves it until it heals the second time; or one does not go to the tip of the flame, so that the blood frozen in the vein does not flow out, and puts a small piece of linen under pressure.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the patient sees it, let it go and do not hold it tight until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary, draw out the blood from another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is wounded because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of the wounding is that the hairs stick out in sharp hot, until the blood is red; then tie it loosely, so that the vein appears well, then draw out the blood through the cross, not too wide or too long; and let the large holes be stopped, and wound well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, put the hand in sharp hot, and let the blood flow out in sharp hot, until you have enough; and if it is still there, do not put the hand back in sharp hot, because it puts more in than before; and the wounding of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the savior of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: strain the hand, and boil in hot water until the blood is drawn out, if one sees it; and if the salve goes against it, and if you apply it all over, it will not hurt anything; and do not remove it too quickly, for the nerves are all exposed to the cold, and then put the hand in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary for you, put oil and silk over the wound to sew quickly, and thus do for each part.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The remedy for the left eye is good for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The remedy for the sophen is good for all diseases that are outside the body, such as marsh fevers, retention of urine, and diseases of the joints and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its remedy is that diseases are driven out in a sharp, hot manner, and rubbed on the vein until it breaks, and tied above the joint; and the vein is at the elbow, and through the shoulder many rains go; therefore this remedy is good for a large vein or at the elbow, which moves.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have the healthy ones above the chest, and you are warned of the nerves that are dislocated, and the healthy one crosses as in painting; and let the flames be like this.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot issue from the chest, reset the chest in high position, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if it is necessary to restart the first time, start the second one a little higher, because the veins are salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so make the other side of the chest equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the elbow is at the elbow bone, and its dislocation relieves the pain of the hip, when it is for an arrow.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its sweat is such that the hairs between or bath, and it is strange above the ankle four in twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is good to cover it, for the legs are clean, and it is very easily reopened by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not treat it, then it heals none of those that open or close quickly, and towards the little toe, and warns of the nerves; and correct so much blood as you see, and then release the ligament, and put it on cotton and hold it tight; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction wounds are made of horns, or of brass, or of glass; and ventosation is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is done in two ways: either all at once, or gradually; and suction that is done by pricking and drawing blood is done in twelve places on the body, of which one is entirely on the back; and the others are placed under the neck; and the other two on the sides of the neck; and the suction outside the mouth; and the suction on the shoulders; and the suction above the hips; and the suction on the arms; and the suction on the legs; and the suction on the ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the body, and therefore does not weaken anyone, as is done with the treatment of a vein; and it should not be administered, neither at all heat nor without heat, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity of diseases requires ventilation, or for customs, then we should remove the bandage every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each ten; for there are some who, when they have the need to ventilate, have heavy breathing; and some who feel repletion and dizziness in their face, and in their head, and in their throat; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swallowed the tongue, and reach for blood; and there are some who snore, and see through bloody and discolored things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the month of May, we command them to fast for three hours after sunrise.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sainfoin helps with the headache of the neck … that comes from them, and it is only necessary after the evacuation of all the body; and this fasting is in place of the sainfoin of the cephalic, and it is not necessary for those who are of cold complexion to use, or who have diarrhea, because this does much harm; and for this reason it is not necessary for the nurse to use, nor for those who have or cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often become disoriented, it becomes necessary to apply the cupping glass a little lower due to the doubt of disorientation.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The application of the cupping glass on the neck is instead of the cure for the head and the basilica, and therefore it is good for the narrowing of the pis, and to open the channel of the promon, and to all, and to replenish; and it should not be applied too tightly, for if it holds too firmly, it can cause disorientation or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The application of the cupping glass on the two ribs of the neck is good for the pain of the head, and obtunding, and emigrain, and strangulation, and to the pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is instead of the cure for the basilica; and it is necessary to command the sinner that he put his hand in applying, that he does not press the artery, and does not cause bleeding from blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Wind disturbances under the chin can lead to diseases of the mouth, and decay of the teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Wind disturbances of the shoulders can lead to diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Wind disturbances of the elbows can lead to blood flow from these large veins, and it is commanded that the patient does not move too much in front, because the insides are naked of clothes, and can be exposed to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the back should be used to remove swellings from the foundation, and for diseases of dislocation, and it should be a large and made of metal, so it can properly pull; and by chance, if it is too thin, it may break; and I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg suction cups heal openly, because they attract blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains of the rain, and the marsh, and the bladder, and relieve the flowers; and they are in the two shins, and the two knees, and everywhere they weaken the body after long use, and bring on fever in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	To apply the leech, first place it empty and quickly fill it with suction, then press it firmly and move it evenly, continuing to do so until you see the liver swollen and red, and the blood appears at the mouth of the wound; then stop, remove the leeches, and take care of the wounds in their condition, for there are those who have tender skin and clear pores: it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make wide cuts, and a deep one; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to finely cut through the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very painful, you should prick the third time; and when we want to pull out the arrow slowly and slowly, we should only suck once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to remove much blood, we should suck often; and if the pain is not relieved, we should prick in front, and the end should be that the wound is perceived deeply, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are hard, and who have strong pores, that you use the points of oil vaporizers and dissolving: if it is in this state, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of pennyroyal, or of lily, or of camomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take equal parts of garlic oil, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person who is to be healed has large and wide pores, one should not put any oil on it, but it should be washed after ventilation with high rosewater, or high cold water, or myrtle water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ash, or high rosewater, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive superfluities rise from old wine, or vinegar, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and should not be made to sweat before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and should not sleep immediately after the sweating, and it is good that they wait until they should sweat and while they are sweating.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	If those who are sweating are also feverish, and if they are too weak and inflamed; then it is good that they take cold things, such as gooseberries and endives and leeks in milk, and similar things; and they should drink pomegranate juice, and charcoal, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold constitution should take honey syrup, and aromatic wine between old and new, and a little vinegar, and small pinches of pepper and pigeons; and on the day they are to vomit, they should drink more than they can hold; and it is necessary to give some men once a truffle or muscat before vomiting, or after, to strengthen the main members; and the wine should be subtle, but it is only necessary for those who are very cold to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed on the body to relieve pain are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and on the gout, and on the stomach and the abdomen and the legs and the buttocks, for these members do not suffer much from being sucked on their own, and no one does it except to draw blood from member to member, as we put suction cups on the breasts when the newborn is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the stomach and on the abdomen to soften the member; and it removes pain, when there is an opilation or a stone, if by its attractive virtue by chance it removes the opilation, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus it is done whenever one places it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained viscosity. These suction cups are administered empty for succoring alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes with a hot bath of water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot water or water in which he has cooked harmful herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the pneumatic device administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two inches of width and a half palm of length, and has or costing around the middle one small hole, as to put an needle, and be of copper, sulfur before so that it does not burn the hair when placing it on the limb; and has in the middle a crossbeam of copper or iron, for putting a cushion held, and there are big and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the pneumatic devices of children are different from adults, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this suction cup on the limb: take the wax or linen cloth, and put it inside the suction cup at the cross of the rod that is inside the suction cup, so that the light does not burn the hairs; then put it on the limb, and do as we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes, and remove the suction cup; and take the linen cloth as before, and start again often, if you have the skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, at all times, there is no rod or plug, and it is not administered except when it is full of sharpness, and it is placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sansues are not recommended for use in members where it is impossible to place suction due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in similar members, such as eyes or nostrils, and others; and the quality of the user is such that when you remove sansues that are in wet places without pressure, take them; and put them in a wet place, until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then clean them with blood and suction, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sansues; and when they are smooth and ready, if it is a place where suction can be placed, place it, for this is very useful.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the limb gently, then firmly, very well, and then wipe it; and if the wound is too large after the course of the wounds, soak a cloth in cold linen, and put it on, until the wound is stopped; and if the wound multiplies, put on vitriol broken, or gauze, and similar things, until it stops bleeding; or you put half of pounded flesh on the wound, and let it stay on the limb until it dries to the limb, it will stop now; and if you have more trouble, take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the snakes do not want to take, rub the wound with fresh blood, or you put a needle until the snake bites it, and then place them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will fall; and when you see that they are choking, powder with a little aloe and crushed silk, or ash, so they will now die.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Be careful, dear child, that the foolish man does not see this chapter, for no one has ever seen any of the ancient books or letters; and for this reason, the science is hidden in our land, for I have never found a good one; and I know nothing, except from the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are necessary, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say or prologue of this book the summaries of the word and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and stay on the truth, so that those who are experienced find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or wounding comes to any part, it is necessary to treat the injury on both sides and on both parts, if nothing happens, such as weakness of the body, children, or elders; or if the tense is not very tight, or too cold; and change cold things, that is to say, cold compresses, and chicken broth and goose fat, and do not drink wine, and do not use any heavy meats, and do not fill oneself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of abscess or spreading of matter to the member; then the injury returns to its previous government as it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to apply a moistening poultice of meat that causes large swelling, or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat, and rice, and tests, and piez, and chicken pan, and eggs, and fish, and thick wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the moistening poultice also causes pain and more quickly the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and the infirm cannot be properly healed or soldered according to their nature due to the decay of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but rather, apply pressure above the broken bone with large strong pieces that support and join the member together, until it strengthens as it was before; and do not completely remove the work, and for this reason, it is necessary to apply a moistening poultice of large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And there are various kinds of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the shoulder is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you all kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes around, and another in soaking, like the shape of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture in a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own means, and proper tools in the restoration, according to what memory comes in its place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the bone is twisted, and open well by itself, and it is at the pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting, and the pains are not great, if there is no fracture; but it can still have twisting, or cut, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move it with your hand, but place the following remedies on it, and then gently hold it still.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the fracture that was in pieces is now separated into two parts, you must now set them evenly, as soon as the swelling comes; and if the swelling is hot and comes, do not let any time pass until the swelling is calmed; then gently and carefully set the bone, and it should be lighter than the restoration of the other where there are pieces; then hold it still, as soon as it is properly set.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, if it is a hand or foot, or to your hand if it is small members, or to two cords, or to one cord and to your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are united, you should gently move them in all ways, and guard that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and properly set the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well in your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it is torn beautifully, and do not strain it too much, and do not press it as those who bring it by their work cause inflammation and contraction of the member, as we have experienced many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in place, well restrain the pain that it does not move, whether awake or asleep, turning or otherwise; and keep it securely so that the member feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and it should be put in the correct position so that it feels no pain; and guard that it is put straightly, so that crookedness does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the member broken is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The qualities of the member broken are different in size and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as the arm and leg and similar ones: for those, it is necessary to wrap them with thin linen cloths; and those that are large, such as the thigh and calf: for those, it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and sturdy cloth, because the wide cloths embrace the whole of the large member, and hold it equally from all parts, so that there is no gap; then wrap lightly around the injury, three or four times according to the length of the limb, and hold your hand a little on each part of the cloth, then go above the fracture and hold it less, than the fracture can be moved a little; then soften the cloth a little and a little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another cloth and return around the broken bone; then return to the part away from the fracture, and hold it moderately, neither too hard nor too forcefully, as we have said in the first section above; then place between the cloths linen or cloth strips, until they are all even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is inflammation or abscess, put something soothing on the abscess and what removes the inflammation, and leave it like that for some time; then strain it with a piece of cloth, or a stick made into clips, or a palm leaf, and they should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the cloth that one puts on the wound should be a little larger and broader than the others; and it should also be as long as it needs for the member of smallness or greatness; then strain it with the cloths as you did in the first layer, then tie it above a thread evenly, as you did in the first layer on the broken part; the tighter it is, the less; and it should be that the threads are neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be of linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of the people who make their bandages from linen threads twisted wrongly, and it is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should only have between each cloth half a finger's width of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are closed by the tips of the needles after straining in their clean state, then put them out of the cloth or other lint, so that it does not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the stitches are broken, I will tell you the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And do not strain all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, do not put needles in them until after five or seven days, or more depending on your risk of abscess; and get the method of ancient plasters to restore breakage, dislocation, and twist: and take some flour that is kept in the mill walls, and mix it with a lot of egg, and put this mixture, not too clear or too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the restoring plaster for many positions, and especially for women and small children, because it is not too harsh.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to heal fractures and dislocations and twists: take equal parts of bread, lard, flour, aloe, and arabic gum, and mugwort, 10 grams; wormwood and aloes, 5 grams; alecost, 8 grams. Grind them into a powder and mix with honey; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and it quickly heals broken bones, and it is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to heal twists: take mugwort and valerian, 10 grams; wormwood and aloes, 8 grams; bolic armenic, 10 grams. Grind them well and mix with honey or a lot of honey, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to treat joints and bones that are dislocated or broken, to relieve the pain, and to heal the wound and the fracture: take a new bandage, moisten it in oil and heat it, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These bandages do not cure, but they are good for relieving abscesses and properly treating pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat broken bones that cures them: take dried fig leaves and earth partridge leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat the fracture of the bone and to alleviate the remaining pain from the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of wormwood, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are chilled, mix with mustard or vinegar, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to apply more than the first, when an abscess is difficult to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of wormwood, linseed, balm, melilot, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and camomile, of all an equal part; and grind, and mix with mustard, sweet salt, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore it, except for a mixture of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it, dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to bandage that is good for the wound and pain: take musk and chewable horsehair, or feathers of an owl, and vismalve, and silk equally, and grind them, and make a bandage and put it on the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then realign it a little later, and be careful if the hairs do not feel any pain, or if the joint does not move; then do not realign it by force again. And if pain comes to the limb, or pruritus, without rest or inflammation, then hurry, and realign it, and remove the dressing now; and take a light bandage, and wet sponge of sea water, and soak in hot, and lift the limb, until the pruritus ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in hot or rose oil, and tie with a nut, as long as you are sure of no abscess forming; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and it is healed, then begin to apply the subtle bandage again, and a little dressing, and do not strain it so much as before; subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess has spread and turned red and painful and swollen, and you have knowledge of plasters and bandages, if it starts to spread again, as you did first evenly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not come to the limb as we have said within three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, as long as the breaker is aware, and approaches the adjustment of the char above; then hold it more than before, and increase its flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the limb becomes too dry, there cannot be any nourishment coming to it; then apply hot and cold water, every time you remove it, and this should be done daily, and loosen the bandage a little; by this work, then, the nourishment is brought to the limb, and quickly heals what the foolish people do, which torments the limb: this is bad, and if such works are not done carefully, and only done correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of breaking are, and diverse figures, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made by percussion of spear, and the collarbone completely breaks the bone just below it which is outside the bone, as if it were a crack or a fracture; and because of this, this type of break is called «crack».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear pierces the bone from above, perforating it, and this type of break is called «absolute»; and it is the wound of these two breaks, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact of the shield, or puncture or from the shoulder of the spear, or falling on the stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a broken bone that approaches the skin that is outside the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is set in the bone as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason it is called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound made by being struck by an arrow, or falling, or similar thing, and makes the piece of the bone enter below, and the threads are like those of a hat when they are sewn on the hot irons; then the arrow enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are more who have or the main bone moist, such as the child's head; and they have all these ways of fracture that small pieces are dislocated as these; and I will speak to you about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of fractures by the removal above them, and the examination with tent, and the corruption that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known because when one has discovered the bone, and one rubs it above, if there is an open fracture black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, be careful of accidents of evil, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes issuing forth and reddening, and other similar things in many positions, if it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see any visible injury, and you hope for healing, then begin treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes first to you, and it is in the leg, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day, so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spine, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, as long as the flesh around the bone is not rotten, and the injuries that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes close to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you remove the part that is torn in such a way: and it is that you hold the head of the painful wound, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound as softly as you can, and if blood comes out when exposing the bone, or an abscess forms, help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the wound with soft cloths soaked in red oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is relieved, and make sure that no blood comes out; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to the two methods of work: one method is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And in the second method, have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be sharp and made of iron in one piece; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the tooth is hard and out of position, it is necessary that you drill around it, as long as you administer cuts with taps, not making it go beyond the bone of the jaw, and should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each one comes in its own place of the bone, so that you have taps for all bones; and this is the form of the three methods of cutting.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for perforating around the broken bone are that you place the tarry substance on top of the bone, and turn your hand away from it until you feel that the bone is pierced; then remove the tarred substance to another part a little later, and so do all around, then cut the space between the bones as thinly as you can, lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pliers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perforated and treated the bone, it is advisable to close the openings that remain in the other instruments similar to an incision, but it must be more thin and more subtle than the other incision; and if there remain any small bones, or scales, remove them gently with the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is such as the Galiens describe, which is much safer; and it is said to be very effective, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you uncover a part of the bone where the break is open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you can place the lens-shaped piece of this instrument in its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and it is the part that is in two pieces, so that the cutter is towards the bone; then firmly strike with a small hammer against, so that you lightly tap the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside; if it is against the bone, lightly tap the bone, because one taps too much harmfully, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate through the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to remove those roughnesses, and to scrape off the scales with the subtle razor that you should have in various quantities, in order to manage each limb in the most suitable way, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have great razors, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair clippers and subtle fractures, it is necessary to manage them according to their location; and this is a thing that is not replied to by the one who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is exposed, it is necessary to apply a cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as possible, so as not to irritate the wound, then administer by pouring over another liquid, and do not strain it except until the wound is healed; leave it in this way for one or two days, until the abscess has subsided, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lis roots, flour of seeds, powder of frankincense, and aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer medicines without biting; and keep the wound clean, so that you do not leave any bandage, because when the bandage gathers on the brain, it causes the head to rot and become very painful; for when something is placed on the wound that bites, it does not help.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	When no accidents happen to the limb, as we have said, it is uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no other harm comes except from the medicine that has been applied, which has power, then you should apply a part of honey, and three parts of red oil and one cloth, and put it on the wound; then cure it with various methods of treatment until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	That never both bones of the forearm above are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and that one is cartilaginous, and does not break easily, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.
