And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you bandage your little finger or thumb on the side of the break, and place it inside the hollow of your index finger, and in the palm by default, until the bone regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and guard that the hairs do not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone, and cannot be brought to the finger, it is necessary that you place it inside the head of a small, slightly larger nail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in both parts, make another one, and hasten to restore the first joint, if you can; if not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling of the wound has subsided, then bandage the head of the finger with linen cloths, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you move to another side, where the break is, and the tents are so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said no one should oil the tents every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it should be oiled with a mixture of honey and powdered charcoal; then leave the tent until the bone is hard and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never use feathers in place of tents, and if there is a soft cloth around, hold the fracture and blow the pain away; now do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are working, put a piece of wool soaked in red oil or a drop of ichthyol on it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If abscesses do not come to the nose, apply a poultice of mustard flour and powdered frankincense, mixed with egg yolk, then place light cloths on it and do not tie the nose tightly; if the broken piece of the nose is small and in many pieces, remove them with suitable instruments, then cut out the wound, and treat the injured parts as appropriate, and sew or cauterize as suitable for the case; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat with tents and apply bandages until healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured, and there is no wound elsewhere, and the fracture is not completely broken, but only slightly cracked, so that one can feel it inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right part, you should push your right index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left jaw, push your right index finger, and gently push the fracture inside, and press it against the other hand outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is in two, then it is necessary to administer traction of two parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or breakage, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place them on the broken jawbone, and place it on a double cloth; and place on the cloth a large well-made stick, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and tie it to the mouth so you can, and command the patient not to move, and give light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the alignment changes, then release the patient from the splint, and then reset it to its original position; and apply a poultice with abundant flour or semolina powder, after you have removed the crust; and place a light bandage over the poultice, and if the poultice becomes hard, and the alignment does not change, leave it until it is healed; often healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses appear, follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, remove none of the bone that is broken; but gently remove the broken pieces with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, expand it according to your need with fire.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have removed all these pieces, and there is no more delay, if the wound is wide, place some healing plasters on it to prevent infection until it is healed.
de la forcele	from the flint
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The flint is broken several times against, behind the shoulder, and the breakage is in three ways: either it is broken and split into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a breakage with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And when the break is without a wound, have two assistants, one to feel the broken bone; and the other to stretch the neck towards the affected part; then set the break evenly at your discretion, so that it forms as it should, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a rounded round cloth or linen ball on the misaligned shoulder, and make it as large as your needs; stretch and lift the broken bone, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you set the break evenly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the shoulder blade with your hands, because it comes out in front, then you must push the hairs aside and place a pillow under the shoulder and support the arm on the other side, until the bone of the shoulder blade is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then approach the fracture with your fingers, and if you find broken pieces, it is necessary to cut through them; and carefully remove the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined for any reason, then use one of the instruments you have; but place the tool away from the shoulder blade to guard against infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It seems like a spoon, and is not quite straight, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work; and have two prongs, as you see, and one wide and the other narrow, as the gap in the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of an abscess, if you cut the wound, and if the gap is small, or you doubt an abscess, then use the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, if you soak the cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The application of the bone, whether it is painful or not, is that you place the plaster of the flour from the mill and some wheat flour on the bone, and put light dressings on, and place a sphere outside the joint, if you have the skill; then take a very great bandage of a palm's width, then place the doubled cloth and the plaster on it; then take a subtle staff of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the head of the bandage is hanging down; and place the staff on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the collar, and remove the sphere from outside the joint, and remove the sphere from the bad part; and splint each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the staff evenly, and you see clearly that the staff does not move above the broken bone, reward it every day, and when the joint is healed, support it; place the bad part on its back, and put a small piece of cloth outside the joint to lift the dislocation in the shoulder, and keep it there for 20 days; then continue with the plaster, if you see that it has skill, and strain and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in 28 days, and less to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	There is not often that the shoulder breaks or moves out of place, except by direct impact; if the fracture appears according to its figure, and it is reset according to its natural form, in all ways you can; then put powder from the mill with abundant honey on the bone, and light bandages, and put over double linen; then put on a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is not even on any part of the shoulder, use a strip of linen so that the splint is evenly pressed; and then firmly bandage all around, so that the splint does not move from its place, and check every day whether it is healing; and every time it breaks, re-bandage and keep it even if it is out of place, and press the pain on its side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 30 days, And when this number is completed, remove and be careful, for it is not bone that heals quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone is pushed before the wound, and not removed immediately, then make an incision, and remove the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the finger to relieve abscesses.
de la brisure dou pis	of the broken finger
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The fingers are never broken in the middle, but this rarely happens; but they often break at the joints.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines to the side, and the pain is great, and there is no movement, and everything, and by chance blood flows, and the tendons are exposed in the broken bone, and the smell is bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the hairs are gently placed over their backs, and the bandage is placed between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulders, and bring together the ribs of both sides to your hands, and subtly put them even in all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place plasters and dressings on top of the thin layer of salt, or other light material, and wrap it in a bandage, and tie it over the broken bone so that it does not move; and return the limb to its rounded position at the back, and gently hold it in place, and rub it every hour with the oil, and if it moves, hold it; and if it is necessary to remove it for corrosion or for itching that comes to the skin, or pain or abscess, then hurry, remove it, and clean the plaster, and apply what has come from methods of treatment; then reapply the plaster, and hold it in place until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The rib fracture does not come forth except in great force after the back, and at the top of the chest, and they only break because they are sharp; and it feels bad during questioning.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster, and the bandage of a splint, if you know how to do it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the rib fracture is inclined inward, it feels great pain and tenderness, like from pleurisy, because the ribs do not touch the cloth; and it must be splinted, and everything wet with much blood, and this is a severe illness, and the old ones have put great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say it is necessary to administer swelling foods that inflate the stomach, in order to bring the broken bone back into place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this mistake, unless chauffer has come, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then the sane.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that none of those who put suction cups on the limb, for proper drainage, and this is reasonable; however, doubt arises because the suction cup does not attract the excess from the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that none of those who should cover the limb with linen cloth in hot oil, and then put tents between the ribs to equalize the lung inside, then treat the cure of pleurisy, of food and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pain is great that they cannot bear it due to the bone that does not pierce the skin, and there is doubt, then one should cut across the broken rib on the side, and one should put a tool to keep the wound open; and then one must saw the bone, and gently pull it out, and then suture the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat them with ointments, until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes out, put moist cloths on top of oiled rose petals, and place them on the wound; and treat it while the wound heals from the abscess, and let it lie down beside or over the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neckbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is never a breaker of the neckbones, and only sometimes does it rain; and similarly at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take note if their hands are softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is often fatal in many positions, and if they move and feel well when they are held and not moved, then the bone joint is saved, and the pains are cured, if it is treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing comes to the spine in the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, if you notice that the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in the hands are present, and there is a sensation of ventosities and egestion without volition; and when it is placed on its belly, if there is egestion without volition.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is placed on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is dangerous: do not try to cure it.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to it, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the care is that you reward if there is an abscess, put rose oil or chicken fat on the spike, as long as it is soothed; then put on one of the healing plasters and drying, and tie with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where you feel the pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dry, it is necessary to cover it with the cure; then remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, to a seam, then treat the wound with char, as long as it is healed; and if the bone is broken, which is called the «bone of the knee», if you have a bottle of your right hand, and put it evenly on the other hand to your power, then put the plaster and the bandage on top, if you are skilled; then stretch it, and if there is dry bone, do it again, and remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs of the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the ribs of the back are broken, and if it does, it is not often very painful at the neck; and if it is long, and declines to the side, and comes to the shoulder, causing great pain, swelling, and bruising where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, until you are above the fracture; and cut away any fragments of the broken bone and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the neck, then set it straight until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it inclines to the inside, then make the patient lie on their back, until the restoration of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, then place the plaster on it, then place a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the fractured part so it does not move; and fill the wound with gauze, until it is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their sound side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess forms and it does not burst, then do not touch it until the abscess is relieved, and follow the method we have already mentioned; then return to restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is located between the neck and the top of the shoulder. If it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two methods: one method involves taking a piece of meat with a single sharp edge, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two broken pieces together and lift them up, and cut into the painful area above the seat; then pour the meat over the broken arm, as far as it can reach, and have a small hook in one hand, then lift any heavy object or the assistant extends it down; then place the broken bone in the patient's hands together, until the patient returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to soothe the pain by pressing it against his back, then command the two assistants that one ties what is above the broken bone at his hands, and the other ties below all the limbs, and stretches each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, then hold the limb away from the broken bone, above and below the broken bone, and stretch each assistant to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the broken bone is near the shoulder joint, then you should tie the middle part away from the shoulder, and the other towards the back, away from the broken bone; and similarly, if the broken bone is towards the back, then you should lightly tie it, without causing pain, until the broken bone is even with the shoulder and the back, then set the fracture as it should be, and hold it still, if there is no dislocation.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes, do not hold it for more than seven days, and put milk and rose oil on it until the abscess is calmed; then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you put the bandage on the swollen part, then bring the arm up with the support, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and hold it with the support, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and put a wider and stronger splint on the fracture than the others, and have two inches of space between each splint; and each splint should be so large that it passes three fingers on each side; then hold the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter, with more force and less distance.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the splint, and the strapping, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess has healed, leave it to be tied up every three hours, as we have said; then examine each joint, that pruritus does not inflame or come to the limb, or the scarring does not come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the pain, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come, then wait until after three hours or more, and let the pain sleep on its back, and have its hands on its stomach; and put the remedy on the injury with a plain cloth of wool equally, and examine every hour of the day or night, that the appearance of the broken member does not move, or the bandages are not softened; if the pain decreases by the power of medicine, and give it the food we have put before, in such a way that the food is at the first subtle; and when it begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg dislocations should be reset every 40 days, and then one should apply and administer hot compresses and medicinal ointments for the limb to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the structure is crooked and swollen, it may take 1-2 months to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, called the "fosciles", where one is small and is the one that forms the wrist; and the other is large, and is the one that is outside, near the little finger; perhaps the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small fractures are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when large fractures are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small fracture that is broken alone, then it should be slightly extended and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large fracture, then it should be stretched more forcefully; and extend it over the cushion, and tie the hand pouch higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the pain cross over itself, and the cushion in front of it higher, so that the pain does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers some arms to the part outside of its hand, or to the other, and other ministers to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the mirror evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is none that can be held by hand, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the broken one there is a wound, I have spoken to the surgeon about it; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration there is an abscess, then glue the cloth made of rose oil and white wax, which is not too soft or too hard; and bind the cloth subtly, until the abscess is soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cast, and apply the plaster of powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, then place the splints, and set the broken bone back in place, a bit wider than the others; and make sure it has six splints or more in various positions: whether the broken bone is in one of the bones, or in two; and hold it above the break, and always less distant, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are above the break be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp; and let the thread, from which it is held, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the limb and the joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you raise the limb in hot water, until those itches are soothed; and let the limb rest without being tightly bound.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then begin the restriction again, and if the joint is broken and the bones decayed, and similar things, then advise.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it a little, and let it rest for some time, until the swelling has gone, and then apply the restriction.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient's harm within twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if they are asked inside, then one can place their hands on their neck, and keep their neck straight, and avoid movement and stretching, and sleep on their back; and it is said that this broken bone is restored in thirty years or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty years, according to the constitutions and the virtues of the compositions.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	It is said that at the back of the hand and on the palm there are few broken bones, and it does not happen often.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plantar ligament of the hand is broken or torn, it is necessary that the hairs be cut straight and evenly; then place the hand on a flat surface, and extend the bones that are broken, and put them evenly in their place, until they are well joined; then apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then put a splint according to the size of the limb; and let it be covered in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is on the outer side of the plantar surface of the foot, make a sphere of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against the broken part of the foot; then wrap it in a long piece of cloth, and put the splint that is as large as the foot of the hand, and apply it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, it is necessary to place one splint above and another below the hand, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it entirely around the arm, and stanch the joint between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fractured bone comes to one of the two, whether it is the thumb or the other, straighten it as it should be; and strain with the palm, and if you see that you must place a straight small splint to lift the fracture and not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, straighten it and bind with the sound finger that comes after; or you tie them all together, which is best, or you place a splint above, as you would for a thumb; and take care in restoration and arrangement of abscess, and heal what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken rib
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bones of the ribs are often broken, and one can see when they return in front and behind; and the restoration is as one puts the bone above the breaker, and the other outside.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the hairs grow on their face, then each minister stretches his share equally; and it is when the breakage is placed in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the breakage is close to the root of the rib, then one of the bones towards the base of the horn, and the other bones outside the breaker.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the glenoid, and then one of the bones towards the glenoid, and the other extension down; then put the mirror the bone even in both hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster, and the bandage, and do not apply if there is no need.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess that needs to be lanced, let it rest first, then return to your work and care; the process is done in a similar manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap the fractured bone in two or three layers of bandages, and let the excess remain, then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the foot, and tie a long piece of cloth between the thigh and the leg, on either side of the knee, and bring the end of the cloth up; then turn back over the leg and thigh, and tie the broken bone, then place a splint on the bone of the leg; then apply the bandage between the leg and thigh with soft cloth to equalize the pressure, then begin to bind three or four times above the fracture; and as you go higher than the fracture, and less tighten; then examine the two ends of the cloth that you have tied between the leg and thigh, and the three splints above, then return to the top of the cloth, until you reach the knee; and if it does not move from its place, then leave it so, then if there is no abscess or swelling, etc.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it has, if the dislocation, and release what comes, as we have said many times; and if he has pieces of bone that can be felt, it should be removed, if possible; and if not, it is necessary to break the limb, and tear away the flesh; and the cure as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the shoulder broken in such a way that these are placed, as in dislocation and the arm; however, in such a restoration made does not hurt the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And so that the shoulder is restored at different times, a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the road of the gout
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	In the road of the gout, there is little breakage, but it often rains.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a small crack or hole, and it has to do with all wounds, and without wound, and it feels very badly.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts together what is broken to its two parts, as much as it can be assembled, then put on the plaster, and if you have the skill, put a round bandage, and hold it as it should be, then warm all the preparations that we have said in other breakages, such as abscess and similar; for each accident that it needs, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" on the right side, and the other is called "foscile"; and they break in the same way as the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm evenly, and the work is all there. And if both bones are broken at once, the leg returns to its original shape.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bones are broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen clearly; and it turns out of place.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and make it even, and tie the tendons equally; but if there is a fracture and it is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and treat according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that gird the leg on one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee to the foot; then wrap them above and below, and tie them in the middle as well, and at this point the leg will not bend to the right or left, and it is well; and no one administers the long cloth of the leg, and it is made of cloth, and properly put on the leg to prevent movement, and correctly done, one checks every day the leg to see if there is an abscess or other accident; if the cure is as soon as they are healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot never fracture and are strong, and there is no weakness in any position.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then put them in a position where they are on top of each other, like if it wanted to walk, and then place your foot on its own, where the bones are raised, then press them so much that they return to their usual position; then apply the ointment and poultice on top, and put a small tablet of two drachms of chalk powder inside the sole of the foot, then bandage the foot evenly, and other things that you have to do.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you release the joint, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any of the two broken, if you restore them as we have said for the two fingers of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the bone, and slightly wider, then place the bandage as I have said, and strain it gently; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, place a splint according to their quantity, wrapped in a piece of linen, and strain the bandage from underneath the bone, so that it presses well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, as we have mentioned; and treat each accident as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the finger bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of childbirth are broken, if the woman is seated, then widen her, then incline her to the part of the back, and hold her from behind; then fill the wound with cotton, and put in as much as possible; then raise the woman, and lift the back slowly and slowly, and at that time the cotton will come out through the natural opening, and the bones will return with it; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and thus do this for seven days or so: then the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of wool, and tie it to the bone with a thread, and blow all the wool into the natural opening; then blow into the thread until the wool is inflated inside: nature will restore the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it in place for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, if it is reset as we have said in the bone of the shoulder; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and his use to it, and pays attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means in many cases the right way of restoration: understand this then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the wing, when it is broken, take a goose quill and blow on the wing; then wrap it in cloths, and leave it for three days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleansed immediately, so that the cleansings that we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, and if there is no other remedy, then begin to restore the fractured bone in the same hour, or the next day, unless complications arise.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if complications arise, then leave the restoration until the next day, until the complications are calmed, and do not touch it on the next day or the day after, for you will bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the jaw is broken and appears to be displaced, then it is necessary that you gently place it in your hands, extending it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not equipped with a tool that can be held in your hands, then use an iron instrument that is seven or eight spans long, and its width depends on the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the mire to hold three or four, according to how much he has in each treatment of the fracture; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not press too much on the member at your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick in the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called «palainche», because the patient must have the broken bone placed on top of the head of the visible bone; and the bone is struck once, as much as it regains, and they are evenly aligned against each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is thin, and the instruments cannot well take the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone until the instruments have capability.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then you must use a suitable tool, such as an iron or saw, to your power; then scrape off what remains in the bone of roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the pain is great after, make sure it is not still in its unnatural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is in its natural position, then clean the wound with black stiptic wine, and properly if it was in a suppurating state; and do not put anything oily on the wound, such as cerote or other things, so that there is no attraction of pus and corruption; then administer these things when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the entire dressing according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not compressed with the breakage; and many times this has been done by foolish people, and they have brought about pus or death or corrosion in no time; and let the straining be less and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that no evil accident has occurred, as we have said, and you relieve pain at the limb, if it does not require to be put in elevated position; but wrap around it, in place of elevating, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is not healing, remove what you have put on top of it, and apply a healing ointment, such as tetraformacon and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you move the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, as long as it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be aligned in some manner such that the bow can move lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the bones continue to protrude, and it cannot be healed but remains dislocated bow, then you should cut off the small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you remove all those pieces that cause such pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if the fistula comes to the limb, or some other manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what it says in its chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open through the limb, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not remove it immediately, for many times it dies within 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come from the healing
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the broken part, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the misaligned shape of the limb; and perhaps it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, if it is fresh: if you administer stiffening medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollis, acacia, and similar things, so that you include none of these things, or all together, and mix them with stiffening wine or with abundant honey or with garlic; and place it on the nail in an enema, and hold it tightly, and do not remove it in the hands; then loosen it, and start another one until the dislocation is removed; or you hold against a piece of smooth leather well made; for the property of the leather is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the dislocation has become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, if the cover above, and make the excess apparent; or you reset it with any razor until it is removed, and care for it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb that is after the siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and it remains after the limbs are weak and thin, there are many causes: because one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and could not come to the proper fittings to the limb; or by multitude of swelling; or by too great movements, not in its time; or because it has little blood in its body, it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the pain less, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and administer baths, and give joy and rest; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great fitting, and the swelling often of high heat, until the fitting goes to the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is deformed, but it does not affect its natural function: if one does not believe the people who say that one should break the limb completely anew, and many have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and great harms come from it, and perhaps the death of the patient; nevertheless, if the dislocations and twists are fresh, it is necessary to apply heated water, or softening herbs that are boiled, such as willow bark, roots, and marshmallow, and similar things; and the mollifying plaster, such as well-made diaquilon, and you take the willow bark powder, and mix it with chicken fat or sunflower oil, and make a plaster on top; or you take figs that are greasy, and grind them with linseed, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation caused by continuously and repeatedly rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And every hour, you should reduce movement in the affected limb.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awake and hardened, like a stone, and it needs to be removed with a knife, if it is necessary to cut into the bone, then make a slight and delicate incision; and put on a bandage and treat it.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, then it must now be returned towards the shoulder.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, if the shoulder swells, and perhaps if it is reset to the elbow; for it does not matter that one moves it to where it is swollen: many times spasms and other pains are brought on; therefore, when this happens, first soothe the injury, then leave it, until the abscess is quieted; then raise the limb with hot and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as the cure comes in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder joint from the elbow to the wrist.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There is also the case where the mandibles are dislocated and the dislocations of the mandibles occur in two ways: either they are slightly offset from their place and slightly softened; or they are completely displaced, hanging downwards, and covering the lips so that they cannot hold them, nor can they close their mouth, and wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns to its place in several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if she is whole and complete, it is necessary that you reset her urgently, and do not delay; and in such a way that the healer pours water on the bad place, and puts the tip of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand is outside, to hold even; and command the patient to soften his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the tip of the hand moves evenly until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to return, immediately if they are both jaws together, then raise the edges of high hot and oil, until it is lightly reset; do not delay the return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned evenly, and the jaw with its bad tooth is well clotted to soften, put a cloth soaked in warm oil and wax over it, then lightly bind it with soft bands; let the painful tooth lie on its back, and its jaws should be between two cushions, so that it does not move to the left or right, nor make any effort to chew, but take light food, until the pains are gone, and the jaw is healed; then change what it wants to eat lightly, and do not force it to open its mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset to their proper position within an hour, and they are not converted back to their normal alignment, then fevers and sweating become customary, and possibly diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then it is certain death; and many times those who have had it die within four days.
de la forcelle	of the wrist
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The wrist cannot be dislocated from the side of its own length and below, and it is not reset once displaced, and it is well felt.
