Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient bends his back and extends his arms; then press the dislocated joint firmly into your palm, and it will return; then put on the bandage and the binding, and hold it in place; and the patient who is on the side cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is displaced once, then reset it to its proper position, as we have said; then put on the bandage and the binding, and hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus the same method is used to restore the patient who has been dislocated from the shoulder.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder is dislocated: one is that it is dislocated towards the back of the shoulder blade; and the second is towards the little finger side; and sometimes it is dislocated upwards, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inwards for the nerves; and often it is dislocated outwards towards the shoulder blade, especially to those who have little flesh, because to them it is very painful; to those who have enough flesh, it is dislocated easily, and it returns easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they are struck or crushed, and the shoulder swells up with an abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must examine him, until you are sure; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation is when it is bent towards the shoulder, and it differs between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a difference between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a groove, and below the shoulder the top of the shoulder, like as if it were a broken bone; and the evil cannot put its hand to its nose, nor move from any movements; and also, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly below; and this kind of dislocation is only to be reset when it is new, or if the pain is severe.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the ministers lift the hand of the dislocated joint upwards, then place their fingers under the joint, and forcefully move the joint back into place; then the ministers lift the hand, and extend it upwards, and put it back in place quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come back into place as we have said earlier, then it is necessary to soak the joint in hot vinegar; and the minister should apply a warm, softening, and soothing poultice made from a decoction of aloe, fenugreek, and melilot in hot water, and apply it to the joint; then the joint should be laid on its back, and a cloth of equal thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the joint, then the foot of the dislocated joint should be placed on top of the cloth, and the minister should gently lift the shoulder and draw the hand away from the joint; other ministers should wet the head of the dislocated joint so that it does not move back; this shoulder is now back in place, and if you see that it has been reset correctly, then you should make sure that the person who is larger than the dislocated joint is standing to the side of the affected shoulder, and pull the shoulder away from the joint, and lift the joint upwards, so that the dislocated joint hangs in the air; and other ministers should draw the hand of the dislocated joint down towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the pain is too light, it cannot be moved with anything heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting can also be done in another way: and it is that one places a long stick in the earth, which the patient should also be held like a spear, and neither too heavy nor too heavy; then it is placed outside the pain, but with a soft cloth over, and the joint should be stretched out along the length of the thick end; then one's hand is placed on the other side firmly, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick of two arms and four fingers wide, which has the top to enter into the mouth from outside the jaw, in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie above the injured shoulder with soft cloth that does not cause the pain, then remove it from the shoulder of the injury; and extend one arm over the long one, and tie the injury on the long arm, and the other hand at the head of the hand, then put the arm over the wide blade of a knife, and let the hands hang down on the other side: the joint is now healed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is healed in any way, you should put a soft cloth bandage under the shoulder, then apply the poultice with flour from the mill, with incense and a little oil, all over the shoulder and around, then remove the bandage under the shoulder evenly, and return the limb to the poultice, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he change little, until the member is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then change more after four or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is strong from moisture that has come, or for another reason, it is necessary to administer cautery at three points, as it is placed in front or in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot be raised above the arm, then cut the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and cut that the joint has never been fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the little finger and the thumbs, or behind, is made by impulse, and extension of hands, and there is another remedy; and treat until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the member becomes swollen and moves slowly, then use the hairs many times, until that swelling is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	That the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and repeatedly returns; and it is dislocated from all parts, and especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not repositioned, for one can see and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the misaligned shoulder with the healthy one, let the patient see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is torn, and cannot move the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it as soon as possible when the shoulder blade comes, for if the shoulder blade comes, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is in the back; it is better than other dislocations, and causes more great pain, and perhaps it kills the patient.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend your hand to both of your hands; and his arms are spread, and the hands on either side, and bend the joint at its base, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, then it returns when he doubles his hand over his hand, and holds the root of the palm of the hand which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to the joint, then administer strong extension; and it is that the one who is doing the extension stretches the arm, and holds it with the other one, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each part, then when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when he sees the joint at his hand, if there is any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in place, then put a dry plaster with some ointment on top, and hold it firmly, and put the arm against the back of the shoulder, and leave it for some time, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, then release the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then restart the bandage and the ligament, and leave it like this for some time, until it is firmly set; then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels gripping after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until it is soothed; or put a piece of fat mutton grease on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and make him take a bath; and when he urinates, rub the joint immediately, then put the grease back on, and then make him take a bath; and so do this twice or three times, until it is healed; and if you see, then put a piece of moist warm chaff mixed with butter on it, and strain it on; and it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is lighter than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place immediately after it is dislocated, if the flesh is swollen or there is an abscess nearby.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the return is that you place the hand badly on a table, and extend the fingers of the hand, and place the palm flat against the appearance of the joint, and press it until it returns completely. Then you should check if it is properly in place; then place the hairs of the hand on a table for extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the bad side of the hand on the table, and the doctor places their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is well. If not, apply warm compresses to abscesses, and leave as such until you can restart.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot place it in the joint after some time, the joint will remain twisted; and do not put anything on the bad side until the hand is clean, and cannot be stretched at all: then cut the nerve or artery; otherwise there is no other means than to stretch by cautery over the case, and perhaps nothing else is worth it.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is in place, put the plaster that we have mentioned on top of it, then hold and leave for 3 days, then release and leave like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no pain, then apply hot water wool and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never dislocate the two fingers of the hand at any part, never at the back of the palm or on the inside; then hold the two fingers, and press against the dislocation to the palm as long as it returns, then support the head of the finger, and push it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave for 2 days, and then put it back that day; and tie it as we have said, and release it on that day, and make it move, and reattach it to the bone; and do this often, until it is straight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the inside of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	back dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the back or neck spine is dislocated, and there are many such cases, there is no cure, for the patient dies from the pain.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excretions suddenly jump out of their own accord, and cannot be held, and often the limbs become soft, or the two thighs or the two arms or one, and often the spine moves to the back; this is called «gilbositez»: the cure is that you reward the gilbositez if it comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And the one that comes from falling or from percussions or similar things, they said in the old ways of cures by great words, which did not have much benefit; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the case of the bone that comes from the front, there is no engine or health; and also the one that comes directly to the second rib, and one cannot cure otherwise than that proper one which comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the hairs should be stretched over its face in the first joint evenly, and he should have some strain away from him, so that he does not bleed; then make the bandage at the head in earth form, and the other at the feet, and tie one lace outside the hairs of the bone, and the other as the waist, and as the thighs, and as the knees; and the assistant should fasten the laces, the one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two bandages; and they should be well tied, the bandage as we have said, and the fingers put their palms over the spine properly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a three-legged stool and place it away from the pain, and the hairs should be on the side, and push the head of the stool away from the pain, then put the middle of the stool on the spine; and put the mirrors under the other end of the stool, and press well until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it to the turned one who turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should tie two ropes to the head of the shoulder of one arm, and on either side of the foot two more, and between each rope, inside and outside, a palm of long hair; and in each rope, a nail, or the turned one corrects, and the ropes are firmly on the ground so that they do not move; and between each two ropes, a rope turning, like the turned ones turn, and in two turns two small ropes of a palm of long hair, to turn the turned one; then tie the ligament that is among the tendons to the turned one towards the head, and the other ligament towards the feet to the other turned one, and each minister turns his turned one along the whole ligament, and the masters put the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, apply a desiccant dressing with plenty of honey, then soak, and then place the limb on a table three times its length to support the neck and the part of the spine that is not injured, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle pressure until it is healed; and if anything goes wrong at the end of the healing, you must administer medicines that are softening and soothing, with the remedy that we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never give anything that appears in the back of the spine, and be careful not to have any presumption: by chance it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder do not come out only as dislocations, but rather in four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, and slightly less outside, front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of this dislocation is such that when the injured leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and more open than the healthy one, and cannot bend its knee at the fire; and it is the legs that are swollen with abscesses, because the patient has fever.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes after this is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has it in front are that he stands well on his leg according to completion; however, he does not double over with pain in the groin, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot do so before, and retains his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has it in the back are that he cannot spread his groin, nor double over, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the shoulder is out of place at the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The signs of this kind of dislocation are such that if the dislocation is recent, it will remain in place according to its position, and there is no remedy; and it is not appropriate for it to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is recent, and it is of four kinds of dislocation, you must quickly return the joint, stretch it out and extend it behind and in front, and move it to the right and left; perhaps if it returns, and there is no other remedy.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must apply strong force, and stretch the leg firmly at two hands, or at one hand that is tied above the knee; and some other remedies place their hand under the tail in a similar manner so that they push their hands away from their buttocks, then they bind it with a belt around the waist; and some tie the head of the limb; and extend up and down all at once, until the pain is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to treat its likeness. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is necessary to put the pain on its sound side, then place the lever under the root of the arm, and the limb which is outside the arm, then extend the lever above the arm, and towards the armpit; then take other ministers his arms, and embrace the large arm of the shoulder pain, and extend it to the other side: if it returns to its limb now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you cannot hold the two bones of the misaligned leg together as we have described, then it is necessary to tie them together with a strong rope above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the misaligned leg be stretched out two fingers more than the other; then hang it over the chief of a staff, and let the other arm be hanging down two arms' length from the ground; then command the minister to grasp the neck of the back, and let another minister hang with the misaligned leg, who grasps the back firmly, for the joint is now approaching.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the lower part, then bend the misaligned leg as we have described in the one with gout, and pull the ligament above the misaligned leg properly, and also at the foot; then put two straps, one at the head and the other at the foot, then fold the strap between the backs of the misaligned leg in the correct form; and wrap moist cloths around it, so that it does not become dry, then extend each minister towards him, and the patient put equal to his hand, the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on the flat surface, and press it as we have described in the gibbosity, and cut off the hairs on the affected side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg firmly, as I have said; and place the fingers on the painful angle, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to extend the affected leg downwards, nor to raise it upwards, but it should be as it was when the hip was dislocated backwards, as we have described for the couching on the two hips; and it should be on its side, and the limb extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table; and it will be all right when the affected leg extends its legs, and they are even; then support the knees, and apply the poultice, and the strap of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then release it, and apply the poultice again; and if you see that they are even, then the strap, as before, and leave it for three or four days; then release it, and make the member move well, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: namely, from inside and outside, and behind; but not from the front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if he cannot do so, it indicates that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back against his face, and put his foot on yours; then take his shoulder to your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the shoulder firmly; and another minister extends his foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the sign is that he can bend his leg at the knee lightly; and put the plaster on it, and hold the leg and knee together firmly for three or four hours, then release; and do not work the patient any more until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not at fault, administer strong extension as we have said in the treatment of the back, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the ankle.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The feet are never bruised, and never completely dislocated, and inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the joint is swollen, and tender to the touch at the part where it is dislocated: the pain is slight, and one should gently extend it to the hands when it is bruised only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated from the beginning, you should first put the pain in the correct position, and hold it with the hands, above the ankle; then take the bandage to your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upwards, and beat strongly on the bandage upwards; do this twice, as we have said, bending and taking the bandage; if it returns, it is well; if not, start the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, place the pain on its back above the ground, and firmly press between its thighs, and wrap cloths around it so that it does not bleed from the pain; then hold the hands on the thigh, and other hands extend the bandage to the hands or knee, where they can tie the bandage above the knee; then extend all the hands equally, and the bandages should be held between the thighs of the pain to hold the dislocation when it is extended; then put the hands evenly on the dislocation, and other hands hold the leg clean at the back, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when she goes to the point, put the plaster and press upwards, and the swelling forms, and tie the foot to the leg, and hold the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the joints do not become too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the swelling does not disappear, apply the plaster again; then let it go on the fourth day or the fifth, and defend against the pain for four days; and if it goes before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary that you relieve it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	For the fire cautery, instruct
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they need to be extended, it is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the body or the joint, it is necessary to make the patient sit with the painful part straight up or on a table, and place your hand over what opens these joints, then press firmly, until it returns; and when it is equal and there is no opening, place a cloth under the sole of the foot, then strain it firmly, and leave it for three hours, then release; and let him rest, until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wounds come with dislocations, and one wants to restore them, often the pain is so great that many die: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and not wise in the art, and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and slow, and hard-hearted; at the beginning of things, calm the inflammation, and leave the pain in God’s hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, now reset the member to its place, as soon as the inflammation has subsided; and when the member is in place, then administer things to calm the inflammation, and cure the wound, as it should be, with frequent dressings; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are crushed, remove the osseous fragments, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into the path of fear, according to what I have said, for it is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and your body.
Amen	For the fire cautery
